This approach will be appropriate where those resisting change are in a position of power.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-manipulation-and-cooptation">5. Manipulation and Cooptation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-manipulation-and-cooptation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>"Cooptation" (no it's not misspelled) involves the patronizing gesture of bringing a person into a change management planning group for the sake of appearances rather than their substantive contribution. This often involves selecting leaders of the resisters to participate in the change effort. These leaders can be given a symbolic role in decision making without threatening the change effort.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-explicit-and-implicit-coercion">6. Explicit and Implicit Coercion:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-explicit-and-implicit-coercion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Managers can explicitly or implicitly force employees into accepting change by making clear that resisting change can lead to losing jobs, firing, or not promoting employees</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="group-dynamics">Group Dynamics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group-dynamics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Group dynamics refers to a system of behaviors and psychological processes occurring</p>
<p>within a social group (intragroup dynamics), or between social groups (intergroup dynamics). The study of group dynamics can be useful in understanding decision-making behavior, tracking the spread of diseases in society, creating effective therapy techniques, and following the emergence and popularity of new ideas and technologies. Group dynamics are at the core of understanding racism, sexism, and other forms of social prejudice and discrimination. These applications of the field are studied in psychology, sociology, anthropology, political science, epidemiology, education, social work, business, and communication studies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="team-building">Team building<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#team-building" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Team building is a philosophy of job design in which employees are viewed as members of interdependent teams instead of as individual workers. Team building refers to a wide range of activities, presented to businesses, schools, sports teams, religious or nonprofit organizations designed for improving team performance.</p>
<ol>
<li>The team member: Successful teams are made up of a collection of effective individuals. These are people who are experienced, have problem solving ability, are open to addressing the problem, and are action oriented.</li>
<li>Team relationships: For a team to be successful the members of the team must be able to give and receive feedback.</li>
<li>Team problem solving: An effective team depends on how focused and clear the goal of the team is. A relaxed, comfortable and accepting environment and finally, open and honest communication are required.</li>
<li>Team leadership: Effective team leadership depends on leadership competencies. A competent leader is: focused on the goal, ensures a collaborative climate, builds confidence of team members, sets priorities, demonstrates sufficient "know-how" and manages performance through feedback.</li>
<li>Organizational environment: The climate and culture of the organization must be conducive to team behavior. Competitiveness should be discouraged and uniformity should be encouraged - this will eliminate conflict and discord among team members.</li>
</ol>
<p>Team building is pursued via a variety of practices, and can range from simple bonding</p>
<p>exercises to complex simulations and multi-day team building retreats designed to develop a team (including group assessment and group-dynamic games), usually falling somewhere in between. It generally sits within the theory and practice of organizational development, but can also be applied to sports teams, school groups, and other contexts.</p>
<p>Team building is not to be confused with "team recreation" that consists of activities for teams that are strictly recreational. Team building can also be seen in day-to-day operations of an organization and team dynamic can be improved through successful leadership. Team building is said to have benefits of self-development, positive communication, leadership skills and the ability to work closely together as a team to solve problems.</p>
<p>Work environments tend to focus on individuals and personal goals, with reward &amp; recognition singling out the achievements of individual employees. Team building can also refer to the process of selecting or creating a team from scratch</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="team-dynamic">Team dynamic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#team-dynamic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When assembling a team it is very important to consider the overall dynamic of the team. When building a team, five dynamics are fundamental to team success:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goals">Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The overall goals of team building are to increase the teams understanding of team dynamics and improve how the team works together. Unlike working as a group, working as a team incorporates group accountability rather than individual accountability and results in a collective work product. Team building encourages the team approach to working on a project. Advantages to this approach include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increased flexibility in skills and abilities</li>
<li>More productive than work groups with individual mindset</li>
<li>More beneficial in times of organizational change</li>
<li>Encourage both individual and team development and improvement</li>
<li>Focuses on group goals to accomplish more beneficial tasks</li>
<li>Improved range of team building objectives such as collaboration, communication and increased creative or flexible thinking.</li>
</ul>
<p>Eight (8) effective strategies a leader should employ to enhance team building:</p>
<ol>
<li>Establish clear and inspiring team goals</li>
<li>Maintain a results-oriented team structure</li>
<li>Assemble competent team members</li>
<li>Strive for unified commitment</li>
<li>Provide a collaborative climate</li>
<li>Encourage standards of excellence</li>
<li>Furnish external support and recognition</li>
<li>Apply principled leadership</li>
</ol>
<p>Organizational mission, vision and core values</p>
<p>Vision:</p>
<p>This involves organization developing a clear understanding of what will be its preferred future. This might not be difficult for organizations who have been managing using strategic plan since they can adopt what they have or modify to suit the ever changing trends in technology and innovations in management approaches. To achieve the vision operation plans have to be developed.</p>
<p>Mission</p>
<p>A mission is at a core of why organization do the work they do. This involves developing sound statement about why an organization exists. It reflects purpose and may include some strategy reflection. In health Records and Information Department for example, they have the training mission statement as "To train competent Health Records and Information Technicians who will provide quality health care to the community". However, if and organization do not existing one.</p>
<p>Core values and beliefs</p>
<p>Values are beliefs that are shared among the stakeholders of the organization and form the principles or commitments that the organization members stand for. This is where the behaviors and ideas that are important to an organization are described. The examples are the respect of staff is the most valuable resource in an organization, Professionalism,</p>
<p>integrity and ethic, a conducive working and learning environment, creativity, inquisitiveness and teamwork, equity across different individuals and/or groups in society and Partnerships with stakeholders.</p>
<p>NOTE:</p>
<ol>
<li>At the end of each unit, provide sample questions</li>
<li>At the end of each manual, list references</li>
</ol>
<p>UNIT TWO: ORGANIZATION OF HEALTH SERVICES</p>
<p>At the end of this unit, the learning should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Describe the organizational structure of the Health care system</li>
</ol>
<p>Organization Structure</p>
<p>Kenya's health system has undergone significant change and reform in recent years and with the promulgation of the 2010 Constitution will continue to evolve. Even so, the system will reflect the inter-linked levels of national, provincial, district, sub-district and community. (These levels of local administration are subject to change in line with the implementation of the new Constitution of Kenya 2010, which provides for devolution of both authority and financial resources). The national level is made up of the MOMS and MOPHS headquarters, with the provincial level serving as de-concentrated units of the national level. (Figures 3.1 and 3.2 outline the organization of the Ministry of Medical Services and the Ministry Public Health and Sanitation, respectively.)</p>
<p>The government health service is supplemented by privately owned and operated hospitals and clinics and faith-based organisations' hospitals and clinics, which together provide between 30 and 40 percent of the hospital beds in Kenya.</p>
<p>The functions of the national level are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Strategic planning and policy formulation,</li>
<li>Enforcement of standards,</li>
<li>Ensuring commodity security,</li>
<li>Performance monitoring,</li>
<li>Capacity strengthening,</li>
<li>Resource mobilization, and</li>
<li>Operational and other research</li>
</ol>
<p>The oversight and policy formulation functions are managed through the Ministers and Assistant Ministers. The Permanent Secretary (PS) is the link between the technical,</p>
<p>administrative and oversight functions, while the Director of Medical Services (DMS) and the Director of Public Health and Sanitation (DPHS) are the coordinators of the technical functions of the respective ministries. The DMS and the DPHS execute their functions through the departments in the respective ministries. These departments are further divided into divisions as illustrated in the figures below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purpose-of-health-structures">Purpose of Health structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-health-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The purpose of an organizational structure is to define the guidelines, parameters and the procedural process necessary for a group to accomplish a main objective. For example, the anatomy of an organizational structure is further reduced to the distribution of authority, span-of-control, and line vs. staff structures, organizational height and departmentalization.</p>
<p>An organizational structure organizes priorities hierarchically by means of identifying tasks critical to a group realizing an end goal. An organizational structure may adopt a live structure or a staff structure or both to achieve their main objectives. A line structure, sometimes called a product structure, identifies the activities directly responsible for the organization's main goal, such as the labor involved in making an actually product. A staff structure is the support staff or network assisting the line structures in their goals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-health-structures">Types of health Structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-health-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-health-structures">Functions of Health Structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-health-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Organizational structure of the Health care systems</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-health-care-system">The Health Care System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-health-care-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health sector comprises the public system, with major players including the MOH and parastatal organizations, and the private sector, which includes private for-profit, NGO, and FBO facilities. Health services are provided through a network of over 4,700 health facilities countrywide, with the public sector system accounting for about 51 percent of these facilities.</p>
<p>The public health system consists of the following levels of health facilities: national</p>
<p>referral hospitals, provincial general hospitals, district hospitals, health centres, and dispensaries.</p>
<p>National referral hospitals are at the apex of the health care system, providing sophisticated diagnostic, therapeutic, and rehabilitative services. The two national referral hospitals are Kenyatta National Hospital in Nairobi and Moi Referral and Teaching Hospital in Eldoret. The equivalent private referral hospitals are Nairobi Hospital and Aga Khan Hospital in Nairobi.</p>
<p>Provincial hospitals act as referral hospitals to their district hospitals. They also provide very specialized care. The provincial level acts as an intermediary between the national central level and the districts. They oversee the implementation of health policy at the district level, maintain quality standards, and coordinate and control all district health activities. Similar private hospitals at the provincial level include Aga Khan Hospitals in Kisumu and Mombasa.</p>
<p>District hospitals concentrate on the delivery of health care services and generate their own expenditure plans and budget requirements based on guidelines from headquarters through the provinces.</p>
<p>The network of health centres provides many of the ambulatory health services. Health centres generally offer preventive and curative services, mostly adapted to local needs.</p>
<p>Dispensaries are meant to be the system's first line of contact with patients, but in some areas, health centres or even hospitals are effectively the first points of contact. Dispensaries provide wider coverage for preventive health measures, which is a primary goal of the health policy.</p>
<ul>
<li>Kenya's health care provision and implementation infrastructure include the national teaching hospital, provincial hospitals, district and sub district hospitals, health centres, and dispensaries, community health services</li>
<li>There is also a host of other operators within the private, non-governmental, and</li>
</ul>
<p>traditional/informal sectors.</p>
<ul>
<li>The system is a hierarchical-pyramidal organization comprising five levels, the lowest being the village dispensary and the Kenyatta National Hospital at the apex.</li>
<li>The mandate for supervision, formulation of policies, establishment and enforcement of standards, and mobilization of resources for health care rests with the Ministry of Health</li>
<li>The country has eight provinces divided into lower levels of administrations called districts, which are responsible for delivering health services and implementing health programs.</li>
<li>Under the decentralization strategy, districts form the central pillars of the public health system.</li>
<li>Management of healthcare at the district level is headed by a <strong>District Medical Officer of Health (DMOH)</strong> appointed by the Ministry of Health.</li>
<li>The DMOH is supported by a District Health Management Board (DHMB) comprising officials appointed by the MOH and from local areas, and a professional unit, the District Health Management Team (DHMT).</li>
<li>The DHMT prepares technical advisories and the District Health Plan in consultation with local health actors and the DHMB.</li>
<li>According to the most recent health management information system (HMIS) data, there are over 9470 health facilities across the country operated by three owner systems.</li>
<li>The government running 43% of the facilities, non-governmental organizations (NGOs) 3.4%, and private businesses 37% all other ownership is 16.6%.</li>
<li>The government owns most of the hospitals, health centres, and dispensaries, while clinics and nursing homes are entirely in the hands of the private sector.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structures">Structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="health-service-delivery">Health service delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-service-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="levels-of-service-and-health-services-at-each-level">Levels of service and Health services at each level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-service-and-health-services-at-each-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Six levels of service 1-6</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="level-6-national-referral-hospitals">Level 6 National referral hospitals.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#level-6-national-referral-hospitals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>are at the apex of the health care system, providing sophisticated diagnostic,</li>
</ul>
<p>therapeutic, and rehabilitative services.</p>
<ul>
<li>The two national referral hospitals are Kenyatta National Hospital in Nairobi and Moi Referral and Teaching Hospital in Eldoret.</li>
<li>The equivalent private referral hospitals are Nairobi Hospital and Aga Khan Hospital in Nairobi.</li>
<li>They are centres of excellence and provide complex health care requiring more complex technology and highly skilled personnel.</li>
<li>They have a high concentration of resources and are relatively expensive to run.</li>
<li>They also support the training of health workers at both pre-service and in-service levels.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="teaching-and-referral-hospitals-have-the-following-functions">Teaching and referral hospitals have the following functions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-and-referral-hospitals-have-the-following-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Health care.</strong> Provide complex curative tertiary care. They also provide preventive care and participate in public health programmes for the local community and the total primary health care system</li>
<li><strong>Quality of care.</strong> Teaching hospitals should provide leadership in setting high clinical standards and treatment protocols. The best quality of care in the country should be found at teaching and referral hospitals.</li>
<li><strong>Access to care.</strong> Patients may only have access to tertiary care through a well-developed referral system</li>
<li><strong>Research.</strong> With their concentration of resources and personnel, they contribute in providing solutions to local and national health problems through research, as well as contributing to policy formulation</li>
<li><strong>Teaching and training.</strong> Teaching is one of the primary functions of these hospitals. They provide both basic and post-graduate training for health professionals.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="level-5-provincial-hospitals">Level 5 Provincial hospitals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#level-5-provincial-hospitals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Act as referral hospitals to their district hospitals.</li>
<li>They also provide very specialized care. The provincial level acts as an intermediary between the national central level and the districts.</li>
<li>They oversee the implementation of health policy at the district level, maintain quality</li>
</ul>
<p>standards, and coordinate and control all district health activities.</p>
<ul>
<li>Similar private hospitals at the provincial level include Aga Khan Hospitals in Kisumu and Mombasa</li>
<li>Their personnel include medical professionals, such as general surgeons, general medical physicians, paediatricians, general and specialized nurses, midwives, and public health staff</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="provincial-hospitals-should-provide-clinical-services-in-the-following-disciplines">Provincial hospitals should provide clinical services in the following disciplines:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#provincial-hospitals-should-provide-clinical-services-in-the-following-disciplines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Medicine;</li>
<li>General surgery and anaesthesia;</li>
<li>Paediatrics;</li>
<li>Obstetrics and gynaecology;</li>
<li>Dental services;</li>
<li>Psychiatry;</li>
<li>Accident and emergency services;</li>
<li>Ear, nose and throat;</li>
<li>Ophthalmology;</li>
<li>Dermatology;</li>
<li>ICU (intensive care unit) and HDU (high dependency unit) services.</li>
</ul>
<p>They should also provide the following services:</p>
<ul>
<li>Laboratory and diagnostic techniques for referrals from the lower levels of the health care system;</li>
<li>Teaching and training for health care personnel such as nurses and medical officer interns;</li>
<li>Supervision and monitoring of district hospital activities;</li>
<li>Technical support to district hospitals such as specific outreach services.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="level-4-district-hospitals">Level 4 District Hospitals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#level-4-district-hospitals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Concentrate on the delivery of health care services and generate their own expenditure plans and budget requirements based on guidelines from headquarters through the provinces.</p>
<p>A district hospital should provide the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Curative and preventive care and promotion of health of the people in the district;</li>
<li>Quality clinical care by a more skilled and competent staff than those of the health centres and dispensaries;</li>
<li>Treatment techniques such as surgery not available at health centres;</li>
<li>Laboratory and other diagnostic techniques appropriate to the medical, surgical, and outpatient activities of the district hospital;</li>
<li>They provide a wider range of services, such as basic curative and preventive services for adults and children, as well as reproductive health services.</li>
<li>They also provide minor surgical services such as incision and drainage.</li>
<li>They augment their service coverage with outreach services, and refer severe and complicated conditions to the appropriate level, such as the district hospital</li>
<li>Inpatient care until the patient can go home or back to the health centre;</li>
<li>Training and technical supervision to health centres, as well as resource centre for health centres at each district hospital;</li>
<li>Twenty-four hour services;</li>
<li>The following clinical services:</li>
<li>Obstetrics and gynaecology;</li>
<li>Child health;</li>
<li>Medicine;</li>
<li>Surgery, including anaesthesia</li>
<li>Accident and emergency services;</li>
<li>Non-clinical support services;</li>
<li>Referral services;</li>
<li>Contribution to the district-wide information generation, collection planning, implementation and evaluation of health service programmes.</li>
</ul>
<p>Level 3 Health Centres</p>
<ul>
<li>Provides many of the ambulatory health services.</li>
<li>Health centres generally offer preventive and curative services, mostly adapted to local</li>
</ul>
<p>needs.</p>
<ul>
<li>Health centres are staffed by midwives or nurses, clinical officers, and occasionally by doctors.</li>
<li>They provide a wider range of services, such as basic curative and preventive services for adults and children, as well as reproductive health services.</li>
<li>They also provide minor surgical services such as incision and drainage.</li>
<li>They augment their service coverage with outreach services, and refer severe and complicated conditions to the appropriate level, such as the district hospital</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="level-2-dispensaries">Level 2 Dispensaries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#level-2-dispensaries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Are meant to be the system's first line of contact with patients, but in some areas, health centres or even hospitals are effectively the first points of contact.</li>
<li>Dispensaries provide wider coverage for preventive health measures, which is a primary goal of the health policy.</li>
<li>The dispensaries are at the lowest level of the public health system and are the first point of contact with patients.</li>
<li>They are staffed by enrolled nurses, public health technicians, and dressers (medical assistants).</li>
<li>The enrolled nurses provide antenatal care and treatment for simple medical problems during pregnancy such as anaemia, and occasionally conduct normal deliveries.</li>
<li>Enrolled nurses also provide basic outpatient curative care.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="level-1-community-level-health-services">Level 1 Community level health services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#level-1-community-level-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Network of simple or community-based health care programmes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some sort of community committees is established.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They may be specific health committees, part of development committee, parent-teacher association or some local group.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A person is then selected to attend a simple training course that prepares them to deal with health problems.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They are given a limited No. Of drugs or no drugs but refer people to dispensaries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>May have like 50 households (250 people) or more to look after.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These workers are called community health workers (CHWs), Village health workers (VHWs), helpers, scouts or motivators.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>o Fourtiers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-services-at-each-level">Health services at each level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-services-at-each-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="actors-cadre">Actors cadre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#actors-cadre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health systems: main actors in the arena</p>
<p>Core partners have the following primary roles:</p>
<p>Funders, providers, purchasers, implementers, watchdogs</p>
<ul>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Private / NGOs</li>
<li>Not for profit (e.g. faith-based)</li>
<li>Private for profit</li>
<li>Civil society organizations</li>
<li>Development partners</li>
<li>International</li>
<li>Bilateral</li>
<li>Foundations</li>
<li>Media</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="referral-system-in-kenya">Referral system in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#referral-system-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For ease of reference and use, the guidelines are presented in 3 volumes:</p>
<p>Volume 1: Management Guidelines for Level 1 (Community)</p>
<p>Volume 2: Management Guidelines for Levels 2 and 3 (Primary Care)</p>
<p>Volume 3: Management Guidelines for Levels 4–6 (Hospitals)</p>
<p>UNIT THREE: COMMUNICATION SKILLS</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>Objectives;</p>
<p>By the end of this unit, the learner should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define communication</li>
<li>Explain the Communication process</li>
<li>Outline the channels of communication</li>
<li>Discuss the barriers to effective communication</li>
<li>Explain strategies for overcoming communication barriers</li>
<li>Describe how to listen and question effectively</li>
<li>Discuss how to give feedback effectively</li>
<li>Explain the Direction of organizational communication</li>
<li>Discuss how to conduct and manage a meeting effectively.</li>
<li>Discuss how to manage official correspondence effectively</li>
<li>Explain the role of health managers in Customer Relationship Management (CRM)</li>
<li>Suggest ways of improving communication and CRM to enhance service Quality in Health sector</li>
</ul>
<p>Definition:</p>
<p>Communication is the process by which we interact with each other. It is the flow – transmission and reception – of information, ideas, feelings, attitudes, perceptions and understanding, both verbally and non-verbally, between two or more parties. Communication is much more than the use of words, whether spoken or written. It embodies attitudes, behaviour, dress, body language, style and method of presentation, quality of listening and perceptions, and interpretation.</p>
<p>Communication refers to the process of relaying messages in a way that is effective and results in a response. Communication is crucial in any organization and for all programmes. The communication process is inseparable from the management aspects of an organization and is a fundamental part of the everyday functions of a manager. Good and effective communication promotes teamwork. Personal relationships within a team can be difficult, but poor communication can worsen them.</p>
<p>Good communication enhances managerial and leadership skills, as well as personal effectiveness. Managers must understand:</p>
<ul>
<li>Channels of communication.</li>
<li>Directions of organization communication.</li>
<li>The barriers to effective communication.</li>
<li>Different ways to improve communication.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-a83a347f.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="communication-barriers">Communication Barriers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#communication-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are any aspects of or conditions in a place that interfere with effective exchange of ideas or thoughts. Therefore, a communication barrier is anything that stops a message from reaching its destination. Barriers may be physical or psychological, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Culture, background and bias</strong>: We allow our past experiences to change the meaning of the message. Our culture, background and bias can be good as they allow us to use our past experiences to understand something new. It is when they change the meaning of the message that they interfere with the communication process.</li>
<li><strong>Ourselves</strong>: Focusing on ourselves, rather than the other person, can lead to confusion and conflict. Some of the factors that cause this are defensiveness (we feel someone is attacking us), superiority (we feel we know more than the other) and ego (we feel we are the centre of the activity).</li>
<li><strong>Perception</strong>: Our preconceived attitudes affect our ability to listen. We listen uncritically to persons of high status and dismiss those of low status. If we feel the person is talking too fast, or not fluently, or does not articulate clearly, or is speaking with an undesirable accent, etc., we may dismiss the person out of hand.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="overcoming-communication-barriers">Overcoming Communication Barriers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#overcoming-communication-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As further illustrated in Figure 5.7, ways of minimizing communication barriers include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The use of different communication systems, including formal and informal methods, in order to facilitate understanding between the sender and the receiver of the message within an organization.</li>
<li>The active role of managers in communication, for example in resolving conflict (relationship, task, social) and encouraging shared vision and team building.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="overcoming-communication-barriers">Overcoming communication barriers; -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#overcoming-communication-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="becoming-an-active-listener">Becoming an active listener<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#becoming-an-active-listener" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-8a17cdcd.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Stop talking
Often, we talk more than we should without giving the other person a chance to respond. If we are thinking about what we will say when we talk, we cannot focus attention on the person we wish to listen to. Do not interrupt.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pay attention
Do not allow yourself to be distracted by thinking about something else. Often, we need to make an active effort to pay attention when others are speaking.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Listen emphathetically
Try to take the speaker's perspective. Mirror the speaker's body language and give the person non-judgemental encouragement to speak.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hear before evaluating
Do not draw premature conclusions or look for points of disagreement. Listen to what the person has to say before jumping to conclusions or judgement.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Clarity in communication: It is important to be clear about the subject and stick to the main theme of the topic when explaining it to someone else. It is also important to be well prepared yourself before trying to communicate with another person.</li>
<li>Establish rapport: Because communication is an ongoing process that involves the active participation of all concerned, people communicate effectively when they are at ease with one another. It is important to show interest in the other person, as this is the best way of getting their attention and acceptance.</li>
<li>Encourage audience participation: This is especially important when unfamiliar or difficult issues are being discussed and collective decisions sought.</li>
<li>Avoid ambiguity: The lack of specificity is one of the barriers to good communication. To avoid this it is necessary to be very clear when giving instructions or explanations. Vague statements such as "take appropriate action" or "make suitable arrangements" should</li>
</ul>
<p>be avoided; rather, the instructions should state exactly what needs to be done.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Be brief:</strong> It is best to be direct and to the point and to reinforce the main points with examples if necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Language:</strong> Special terms that may be unfamiliar to the listener should be explained and jargon avoided. If the language being used to communicate is a foreign or second language, it is best to use simple words and sentences, and to verify understanding.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Develop listening skills:</strong> Since communication is a two-way process, it is as important to listen carefully as it is to speak properly. Sometimes we do not listen well for a number of reasons, such as boredom, bias, fear of being influenced and interruptions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Feedback:</strong> Feedback from the listener needs to be recognized by the sender, even when it is non-verbal (example yawning, being distracted, checking text messages). If what you are saying is not being registered or has the wrong effect, change your communication approach.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Timing and situation:</strong> Effective communications requires enough time to cover the subject adequately without unnecessary interruptions. If interruption is unavoidable, it is important to set a formal date for continuing the discussion in the not too distant future.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Verification:</strong> This goes back to the definition of communication as a two-way process involving both transmission and reception. To ensure accurate communication, it is important to ask questions to verify that your communication has been received in the way it was intended and that you heard the message that was intended.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Use of different communication methods:</strong> A mix of formal and informal methods may facilitate understanding between the sender and the receiver of the message within an organization.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-effective-communication">Role of effective communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-effective-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Promotes teamwork,</p>
<p>Enhances managerial and leadership skills,</p>
<p>Enhances personal effectiveness,</p>
<p>(Involve the learner in adding more roles by brainstorming)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="channels-of-communication">Channels of Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#channels-of-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Channels of communication are mechanisms for linking one person to the other/others and vice versa. The channels vary, but those most commonly used to communicate with staff may be divided into organizational and interpersonal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organizational">Organizational<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizational" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Organizational communication is the consideration, analysis and criticism of the role of communication in organizational contexts; it may be formal or informal. For example, written communication becomes important when certain proceedings or instructions need to be recorded and guidelines/procedures need to be followed. Staff meetings may be called to give staff an opportunity to exchange information or solve problems, or to give instructions about a new skill that may need a detailed explanation or demonstration</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interpersonal">Interpersonal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interpersonal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process of face-to-face communication between individuals. Such communication may take several forms. Messages may be verbal (that is, expressed in words), or they may not involve words at all but consist of gestures, facial expressions and certain postures. For example, managers often communicate verbally with staff members on a one-to-one basis to discuss good or poor performance, to motivate and counsel them, to discuss and solve problems arising at the workplace, and to understand better the individual problems of their staff. They may also communicate in writing, to give instructions, get suggestions and document actions for disciplinary purposes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="communication-networks">Communication Networks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#communication-networks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A network consists of a set of interconnected devices, nodes, hosts or computers linked across a communication medium. Communication networks, specifically, are links and nodes especially set so that messages may be passed from one part of the network to another through multiple links and various nodes. A network can offer a choice of services including voice transfer, file transfer, remote login and message passing. Therefore, networks, or patterns, are aspects of direction and flow of communication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direction-of-organizational-communication">Direction of Organizational Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direction-of-organizational-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are basically three directions in which communication operates – up, down and sideways:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Downward communication:</strong> From supervisor to subordinate (e.g., job instructions, information on organization policies, performance feedback, information about the organization's goals and changes).</li>
<li><strong>Upward communication:</strong> From subordinate to supervisor (e.g., grievance procedures, department meetings, participation in decisions, others).</li>
<li><strong>Horizontal communication:</strong> This is communication between/among staff at the same level.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ways-to-improve-communication">Ways to Improve Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ways-to-improve-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once you are aware of all the aspects influencing effective communication, you can begin to enhance your own communication skills. The following suggestions intend to help you to improve your skills in conveying – and receiving – messages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="asking-good-questions">Asking Good Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#asking-good-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Asking good questions is an art that can be learned</li>
<li>Not all questions are good questions</li>
<li>Sometimes they are statements or commands that are disguised as a question for example, "Don't you think you should have done that differently?"</li>
<li>Such inquiry blocks learning</li>
<li>Leading questions also block learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fd2b0b0e">Communication skills – Good questioning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fd2b0b0e" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Inquiry That Encourages Learning</th><th>Inquiry That Blocks Learning</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>How do you see this differently?</td><td>Don't you agree? (especially when said in an intimidating way)</td></tr><tr><td>What's your reaction to?</td><td>Did you do that because of X, Y, or Z?</td></tr><tr><td>What led you to that conclusion/action?</td><td>Do you really think you did a good job? (when you think he did not)</td></tr><tr><td>Could you say more about that?</td><td>Why don't you just try what I'm suggesting?</td></tr><tr><td>Why is that so?</td><td>Why didn't you just tell me?</td></tr></tbody></table>
<table><thead><tr><th>What makes you?</th><th>Why are you so defensive?</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>What kept you from telling me?</td><td>Why don’t you?</td></tr><tr><td>How do you think I/you contributed to that?</td><td>What’s the matter with you?</td></tr><tr><td>How can I/you/we?</td><td>Don’t you agree? (especially when said in an intimidating way)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effective-listening">Effective Listening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effective-listening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Good listening involves an attitude as well as a skill</p>
<p>You have to believe that the other person is worth listening to, has something of value to say.</p>
<p>Listening is difficult when your own mind is busy chattering away or occupied with concerns that have nothing to do with the other.</p>
<p>Listening is hard when you have a strong urge to say something or when you have already come to a conclusion about the other person's problems or issues.</p>
<p>There are three disciplines for learning to listen better.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>focus:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>empathy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>silence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To practice focus, periodically summarizing, briefly, what the other person said</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Ask if that is what she meant to say</p>
<p>To practice empathy, try to rephrase in your own words what you think the other person must be feeling</p>
<p>To practice silence, give time to the other person to think about a question you made.</p>
<p>Practice being silence by not jumping in, counting until 30 if you must, and observe what happens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="feedback-speaking-hints">FEEDBACK &amp; SPEAKING HINTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#feedback-speaking-hints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>FEEDBACK</p>
<p>SPEAKING HINTS</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Evaluative</th><th>Ask listener if they are following your message</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Interpretive</td><td>Give receiver chance to comment or ask questions</td></tr><tr><td>Supportive</td><td>Clarify and look at receiver</td></tr><tr><td>Probing</td><td>Ensure words match message, tone and body language</td></tr><tr><td>Understanding</td><td>Vary tone and pace</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Avoid ambiguity and note signs of confusion</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>PUBLIC SPEAKING
OBJECTIVES
INTRODUCTION
To work on
Effective Presentations Skills</p>
<p>FIVE STEPS TOWARDS A GOOD PRESENTATION</p>
<ol>
<li>Decide what you want to achieve. what is the message?</li>
<li>Decide what form the presentation should take</li>
<li>Prepare a script</li>
<li>Rehearse it</li>
<li>Deliver it effectively</li>
</ol>
<p>Step 1. Decide what you want to achieve</p>
<p>What are you trying to achieve?
Which three messages do you want your audience to take back with them?
What are the arguments of the three messages?
What is your flow?
Identify arena
Nature of event, number of participants, time of day, time available, shape of room</p>
<p>Know your audience</p>
<p>Who are they? What do they know already? How much can you take for granted? Will they understand the jargon?</p>
<p>Step 2. Form of the presentation</p>
<p>Will they understand the jargon?</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-a294a33a.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Step3 Prepare a script (1)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-long">How long?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-long" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Average attention curve max 25 to 40 minutes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="do-you-intend-to-use-slides">Do you intend to use slides?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-you-intend-to-use-slides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>About 2 to 3 minutes per slide</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-much-new-information">How much new information?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-much-new-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>20 minutes: 2 points - 30 minutes: 3 points</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="written-speech-or-cues">Written speech or cues?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#written-speech-or-cues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Step 3: Prepare a script (2)</p>
<p>Structuring the content</p>
<p>Tell them what you are going to tell them. Tell them. Then tell them what you have just told them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="step-4-preparing-for-your-presentation">Step 4: Preparing for your presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-4-preparing-for-your-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rehearse:</p>
<p>How long does it really take?</p>
<p>How effective is it?</p>
<p>How good are my script and visual aids?</p>
<p>Get a good colleague to listen to you</p>
<p>Use your aids</p>
<p>Go through the whole thing</p>
<p>Debrief</p>
<p>If you can, do it again!</p>
<p>Clothes</p>
<p>Before the presentation</p>
<p>Take a timeout</p>
<p>Check your appearance</p>
<p>Run cold water on hands</p>
<p>Yawn, stretch, make faces, blow like a horse</p>
<p>Shake your hands</p>
<p>Remember: You are the person who knows most about what you are going to say!</p>
<p>Step 5: Opening</p>
<p>Find friends – about three or four will do
The first minute is critical:</p>
<ul>
<li>Know by heart the first two minutes of your presentation.
Using hooks or ice breakers – all have pros and cons
Quotes
Humour
Rhetorical questions
Personal anecdotes
Shocking statistics
Outrageous statements</li>
</ul>
<p>Step 5; Nonverbal behaviour
Non-verbal aspects of speech
Tone and colour of the voice
Volume
Rhythm/Pauses
Pronunciation/diction
Eye contact and body
Eye contact
Arms/gestures
Body language</p>
<p>Step 5: Closing</p>
<p>Vital part of the presentation
Common mistakes</p>
<ul>
<li>Cliché</li>
<li>Emergency stop</li>
<li>Endless maze or the more the merrier</li>
</ul>
<p>Consider using "closing summary"
When you come to the end stop!</p>
<p>Visual aids</p>
<p>What we remember:</p>
<ul>
<li>20% of what we hear</li>
<li>30% of what we see</li>
<li>50% of what we hear and see
They should add to the presentation, not distract from it!
They must be clearly visible and understandable!
Speak to you audience – not to your visual aids
Handouts before or after?</li>
</ul>
<p>GOOD AND READABLE SLIDES</p>
<p>Good slides</p>
<ul>
<li>Five to six bullets at the most</li>
<li>Max 6 seconds to read</li>
<li>Use charts or figures where possible</li>
<li>Use large simple fonts (18pt or more)</li>
<li>Use colours (but with caution!)</li>
</ul>
<p>UNIT FOUR: HEALTH ECONOMICS</p>
<p>Purpose:
The purpose of this unit is to equip the learner with knowledge and skills in health economics</p>
<p>Expected learning outcomes</p>
<p>By the end of this unit, the learning should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Describe demand and supply</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the health service/product quality</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the financial accounting systems and mechanisms</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the uses of accounting documents</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the key concepts in Health Financing and resource management.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the sources of government finances and alternative healthcare financing mechanisms</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply the laws and criteria governing public expenditure to allocate and manage resources at the workplace</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the government budgeting cycle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Develop an MTEF and annual budget for a health records department plan.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply appropriate principles and skills to make financially sound decisions in planning and control of financial resources.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Develop a fund raising strategy as part of a departmental project.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analyse the concept of demand and supply in economics and its adaptation in health care.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="discussion-questions">Discussion questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discussion-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>What is health and health care?</li>
<li>What is health economics?</li>
<li>Why is it important?</li>
<li>What makes the health care market different from the market or other goods?</li>
</ul>
<p>What type of questions do health economists ask?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-health">What is health?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health is a multifaceted concept and not easily measurable. WHO defined as definition a state of complete physical and mental well-being and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity (WHO, 1948). It refers to peoples' health status (how healthy they are).</p>
<p>Important part of human capital:</p>
<ul>
<li>Human capital: value of learning, experience and ability embodied in workers which increases productivity and income.</li>
<li>Asset: accumulates and depreciates</li>
</ul>
<p>Individual or households can improve their health through use of health care, diet..</p>
<p>Production of health:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health Production Functions</li>
<li>Determinants of health</li>
</ul>
<p>What is health care?</p>
<p>Definition:</p>
<p>It is the prevention, treatment, and management of illness and the preservation of mental and physical well-being through the services offered by the medical and allied health professions.</p>
<p>Important difference between health and health care is that, health care can be traded on the market but health cannot.</p>
<ul>
<li>Demand health care to improve our health</li>
<li>Demand for Health Care</li>
<li>Health care markets differ from markets for other commodities</li>
</ul>
<p>Roots of health economics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Concerned with the health market not with health or health status.</li>
</ul>
<p>What is health economics?</p>
<p>Economics is the study of how people allocate their limited resources in an attempt to satisfy their unlimited wants. Health economics on the other hand is the study of how (scarce) resources are allocated to and within the health economy.</p>
<p>Basic concepts of supply and demand analysis</p>
<p>Definition of Demand: It is the need and ability and willingness to pay for a commodity - The schedule of amounts of any product that buyer will purchase at different prices during some Stated time period.</p>
<p>Desire: refers to people's willingness to own a good. Demand is the amount of a good that consumers are willing and able to buy at a given price.</p>
<p>Definition Supply: the amounts of a good producer are willing and able to sell at a given price. For many people the word market conjures up a picture of a town square with lots of small stall holders selling everything from fruit and vegetables to meat and fish. For economists, the term has a much wider meaning. It is used to describe any process of exchange between</p>
<p>buyers and sellers.</p>
<p>Formally, a market can be defined as any set of arrangements which allows buyers and sellers to communicate and thus arrange exchange of goods, services or resources. A free market is where such exchange occurs without interference from the government.</p>
<p>Information is a vital ingredient for any market. Both buyers and sellers need to have access to sufficient information to allow them to make rational decisions. So a market for health care must involve two groups: the buyers and the sellers, who interact to trade health care. Who would the buyers and sellers be in such a market? We all want good health and so most of us would be prepared, if necessary, to purchase medical treatment to cure an illness. This suggests that everybody is potentially a buyer (or consumer) of health care. More precisely, at any moment, a buyer would be any body who was ill or who wanted preventative medical treatment such as vaccination or who wanted guidance about their health. The sellers would be those people who could provide medical and health care services, such as doctors, nurses, physiotherapists, dentists and high street chemists.</p>
<p>The concept of supply and demand analysis helps to understand exactly how this spending of money operates in a market system. The answers to these and a thousand other questions can be found in the theory of supply and demand. This theory shows how consumer preferences determine consumer demand for commodities, while business costs underpin the supply of commodities. Finally, we will see how supply and demand are brought into balance by the movement of prices – by the prices.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-9e1a7ee1.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="equilibrium">Equilibrium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equilibrium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When supply and demand are equal (i.e. when the supply function and demand function intersect) the economy is said to be at equilibrium. At this point, the allocation of goods is at its most efficient because the amount of goods being supplied is exactly the same as the amount of goods being demanded. Thus, everyone (individuals, firms, or countries) is satisfied with the current economic condition. At the given price, suppliers are selling all the goods that they have produced and consumers are getting all the goods that they are demanding.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-6c16a21a.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<p>Law of supply and demand</p>
<p>For higher prices less quantity is demanded and vice versa. Moreover, determinant of demand are taste, number of buyers, income, price of related goods and technology.</p>
<p>Law of supply</p>
<p>For higher prices greater quantity is supplied. Supply is always based upon a firm's cost.</p>
<p>Determinants of supply:</p>
<p>An important distinction between Need and Demand</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Needs</th><th>Demands</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Someone's subjective idea (may be based on a formula applied objectively, but the choice to use the formula was someone's subjective idea). Money is not a factor.</td><td>Objectively observable as behavior in the market.</td></tr><tr><td>Money is a key factor. "Demand" is also called "effective demand," because it's expressed only by spending money</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Healthcare financing:</p>
<p>Healthcare financing is much more than a matter of raising money for health. It is also a matter of who is asked to pay, when they pay and how the money raised is spent. This includes raising adequate funds for health, in ways that ensure people can use needed services, and are protected from financial catastrophe or impoverishment associated with having to pay for them. It provides incentives for providers and users to be efficient.</p>
<p>Sources of health care financing:</p>
<p>☐ general revenue or earmarked taxes
☐ social insurance contributions
☐ private insurance premiums
☐ community financing
☐ direct out of pocket payments</p>
<p>Each method</p>
<p>☐ distributes the financial burdens and benefits differently
☐ each method affects who will have access to health care financial protection</p>
<p>General revenue or earmarked taxes</p>
<p>The most traditional way of financing health care finances a major portion of the health care (especially in low income countries) Social insurance. It is compulsory. Everyone in the eligible group must enroll and pay a specific premium contribution in exchange for a set of benefits. Social insurance premiums and benefits are described in social compacts established through legislation. Premiums or benefits can be altered only through a formal political process.</p>
<p>Private insurance</p>
<p>Private contract offered by an insurer to exchange a set of benefits for a payment of a specified premium. Marketed either by nonprofit or for profit insurance companies, consumers voluntarily choose to purchase an insurance package that best matches their preference. Private insurance is offered on individual and group basis. Under individual insurance the premium is based on that individuals risk characteristics.
