Major concern in private insurance is buyer's adverse selection, under group insurance; the premium is calculated on a group basis. Risk is pooled across age, gender and health status.</p>
<p>Community based financing</p>
<p>Refers to schemes are based on three principles;-</p>
<ul>
<li>Community cooperation,</li>
<li>Local self-reliance and</li>
<li>Pre-payment</li>
</ul>
<p>Factors for success of community financing are technical strength and institutional capacity of the local group.</p>
<p>Financial control as part of the broader strategy in local management and control of health care services;-</p>
<ul>
<li>Support received from outside organizations and individuals</li>
<li>Links with other local organizations</li>
<li>Diversity of funding</li>
<li>Responding to other (non health) development needs of the community</li>
<li>Ability to adapt to a changing environment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direct-out-of-pocket">Direct out of pocket<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-out-of-pocket" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☐ Made by patients to private providers at the time a service is rendered
☐ User fees refer to fees the patients have to pay to public hospitals, clinics, and health posts not to private sector providers.
☐ Proponents of user fees believe that the fee can increase revenue to improve the quality of public health services and expand coverage
☐ Major objection raised against user fees had been on equity grounds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-financing">Community financing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-financing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Technical strength and institutional capacity of the local group</li>
<li>Financial control as part of the broader strategy in local management and control of health care services</li>
<li>Support received from outside organizations and individuals</li>
<li>Links with other local organizations</li>
<li>Diversity of funding</li>
<li>Responding to other (non health) development needs of the community</li>
<li>Ability to adapt to a changing environment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-based-insurance-schemes">Community based insurance schemes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-based-insurance-schemes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Primarily for informal sector</li>
<li>Tends to cover all insured members of the community for all available services but have emphasis on primary health.</li>
<li>Most financed from patient collections, government grant, donations, and such miscellaneous items as interest earnings or employment schemes</li>
<li>Most NGOs have their own facilities or mobile clinics to provide health care.</li>
<li>Total coverage is estimated to be about 30 million people (Ellis 1997).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="conclusion">Conclusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conclusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Role of health economists be recognized.</li>
<li>Health financing cannot be dealt separately as it has got to do with good governance, economic growth, education.</li>
<li>Social inclusion and financial protection seems to be provided through community based financing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-funds-the-health-sector-in-kenya">Who Funds The Health Sector In Kenya?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-funds-the-health-sector-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The health sector in Kenya obtains varying levels of funding from the traditional sources: public (government), private firms, households and donors. According to the 2005/06 National Health Accounts (NHA), households remain the largest contributors of health funds, at 35.9%, followed by the government, and then donors, who contribute approximately 30%.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="health-financing-how-much-is-available">Health Financing: How much is available?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-financing-how-much-is-available" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The GOK funds 25 the health sector through budgetary allocations to the MoH and the MoPHS and related government departments. As far as government spending is concerned, the Ministry of Finance sets three year budget ceilings for each sector in Kenya. In practical terms this means that the Ministry of Health creates a budget based on what the Ministry of Finance has said it will allocate for health expenditures rather than submitting a budget request based on actual needs. The Ministry of Health then disburses the funds it receives through its District Health Management Boards. The health budget shortfalls are manifest in the widespread lack of adequate drugs and pharmaceuticals, staff shortages and poor maintenance of equipment, transport, and facilities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="from-the-kenyan-people-cost-sharing">From the Kenyan People (Cost Sharing)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#from-the-kenyan-people-cost-sharing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Over the past two decades, the GOK has pursued a policy of cost sharing to bridge the gap between actual budgets and the level of resources needed to fund public health sector activities. The revenue from the cost-sharing programme has continued to grow in absolute terms and as a percentage of the recurrent government budget. In 2002-03, cost-sharing</p>
<p>contributed over 8% of the recurrent expenditure and about 21% of the non-wage recurrent budget of the MoH. However, because of the worsening poverty situation in the country, the MoH has changed its cost-sharing policy and replaced it with a “10/20” policy, in which dispensaries and health centres are not to charge user fees for curative care other than Ksh 10 or 20 for client cards 28.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="from-the-donors">From the Donors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#from-the-donors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Kenya depends significantly on donor funds, many of which supplement the development component of the national health budget. In 2009/10, on-budget external resources accounted for 15.1% of all health spending in Kenya, or Kshs 7.1 million. In 2005/06, Kenya's health budget was made up to 11.3% by donor contributions. Over the years, Kenya's health sector has increased its dependency on external sources.</p>
<p>All donor commitments for Kenya's health sector—on and off budget—represent USD 99 million in 200831, down from USD 147 million in 2005. The United States is the largest bilateral donor, channelling funds through PEPFAR, the President's Malaria Initiative and USAID with USD 32.4 million in 2008. The United Kingdom also commits significant bilateral funds to the health sector (USD 30 million). When analyzing donors' actual health disbursements to Kenya, the picture looks different. In 2008, donors provided USD 116 million up from USD 102 million in the previous year. The biggest donors were GAVI, GlobalFund to Fight Aids, Tuberculosis and Malaria and the United Kingdom. This graph shows that the US ranks only fifth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kenya-national-budget-process">Kenya National Budget Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-national-budget-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In Kenya the budgetary process comprises three main stages: drafting, legislation, and implementation and audit. Reforms aimed at improving the budgetary process have sought to impose greater fiscal discipline on the government among other objectives such as attaining allocative and operational/technical efficiency. The constitution requires the executive to raise and allocate resources for government projects within this rigorous budget process. The Budget cycle is based on the Medium Term Expenditure Framework (MTEF) cycle. The MTEF process prioritizes definition of a global resource envelope, determination of</p>
<p>inter-sectoral allocations based on core functions and proposals of inter-sectoral allocations based on outcomes, activities and outputs. Public hearings and involvement of private and civil society in the budget preparation enhances transparency.</p>
<p>The MTEF process revolves around the activities of ten MTEF sectors, including the human resource development sector. To guide the preparation of MTEF, the Ministry of Finance issues to all ministries, departments and government agencies in August a circular detailing the guidelines with objectives for the financial year. The Circular-Budget preparation guidelines for budget 2010-11 for example directed that the preparation of the budget for the next MTEF period should be within the context of stimulating growth and creating jobs, reducing poverty and enhancing food security, and protecting the poor and most vulnerable of the society while improving government efficiency in delivering services.</p>
<p>The budget is prepared through Sector Working Groups (SWGs) comprising different ministries, departments, and agencies. The overall fiscal and macroeconomic framework—including strategies, outlook and forecast—determines the role of ministerial working groups (MWGs). The Ministry of Public Health and Sanitation (MoPHS) and the Ministry of Medical Services (MoMS) both appoint representatives to the ministerial working group who then work within the SWG. The two ministries fall under the human resource development sector.</p>
<p>The Sector Working Groups are urged to ensure that they only consider proposals for funding that support the achievement of the objectives and priorities outlined in the Medium Term Strategy of Vision 2030. The Circular from the Ministry of Finance encourages the involvement of districts and other stakeholders in the MTEF budget process through the sector hearings. The purpose of the Sector Hearings is to ensure transparent discussions of priorities of government for the next financial year with key stakeholders including development partners, civil society, private sector and research institutions.</p>
<p>Financial management is the process of achieving the organization's objectives in an efficient manner through planning (budgeting), acquiring, organizing, directing monitoring,</p>
<p>controlling and reporting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-is-it-important">Why is it important?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-is-it-important" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>

<li>Health care market is difference from other markets</li>
<li>Externalities</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="financial-management-in-health-care">Financial Management in Health Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#financial-management-in-health-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-health-financing">Definition: Health financing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-health-financing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Health financing is making funding available to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure choice and purchase of cost-effective interventions</li>
<li>Give appropriate financial incentives to providers and</li>
<li>Ensure that all individuals have access to effective health services.</li>
</ul>
<p>It requires equitable and efficient revenue generation and efficient purchasing of health inputs and services</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-financial-management">Definition: Financial Management.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-financial-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<p>TERMINOLOGIES AND DOCUMENTS INGOVERNMENTAL ACCOUNTS</p>
<ul>
<li>Consolidated fund
A fund where all revenues or other monies raised or received by the government are paid into</li>
<li>Appropriations in Aid
Particular classes of revenue which the Treasury authorities allow an accounting officer to use in addition to the amounts to be issued from exchequer to meet expenditure</li>
<li>Paymaster General (PMG)
The principal agent of the government and is considered as the banker for all government departments</li>
<li>Cashbook
Shows all receipts and payments of cash</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="accounting-officers">ACCOUNTING OFFICERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accounting-officers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>☑ All contracts are complied with; All applicable procedures are followed in the acquisition and disposal of property and that adequate arrangements are made for the custody, safeguarding and maintenance of property;</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="authority-to-incur-expenditure">AUTHORITY TO INCUR EXPENDITURE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#authority-to-incur-expenditure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A controlling officer may, in accordance with the prevailing circumstances incur expenditure and authorize expenditure to be incurred against any provision shown in any subhead for which he is the controlling officer.</p>
<ul>

</ul>

<p>For any purpose within the ambit of that subhead</p>
<p>In accordance with the terms of the allocation warrant.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="financial-regulations-and-procedures">FINANCIAL REGULATIONS AND PROCEDURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#financial-regulations-and-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-they">What are they?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-they" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>These are firm and well defined rules, guidelines and procedures that provide both the institutional and the legal framework for managing and accounting for public funds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="it-takes-two-forms-namely">It takes two forms namely:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-takes-two-forms-namely" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Establishment of Institutional Framework and</li>
<li>Establishment of the legal Framework (Procedures) for dealing with financial affairs of the</li>
</ul>
<p>country</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="financial-management-policies">Financial Management Policies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#financial-management-policies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The responsibility for management, supervision, control and direction of all matters related to the financial affairs of Kenya are vested in the Minister of Finance (Treasury), who discharges his responsibilities through formulation and promulgation of regulations under powers given to him in the Exchequer and Audit Act, (Cap.412).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principal-sources-of-financial-regulation">PRINCIPAL SOURCES OF FINANCIAL REGULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principal-sources-of-financial-regulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Government Financial Management Act (GFMA)</p>
<p>What is a budget? The budget is more than just a number of figures</p>
<p>The budget should express: targets of government policy measures and instruments to reach these targets costs connected to the targets and measures</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="three-elementary-questions-in-the-budget">Three elementary questions in the budget<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#three-elementary-questions-in-the-budget" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>What is it that you want to achieve (what's your goal)?</li>
<li>What measures are you going to take to achieve that goal?</li>
<li>What is it going to cost?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="budgeting-in-the-public-sector">Budgeting in the public sector<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budgeting-in-the-public-sector" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Political instrument to allocate scarce resources to priorities</li>
<li>Managerial tool to explain how programs achieve policy objectives</li>
<li>Economic instrument to influence the economic growth of the country</li>
<li>Control tool to hold managers accountable for outcomes &amp; outputs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="different-budget-formats">Different budget formats<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#different-budget-formats" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="to-draw">TO DRAW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#to-draw" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="1-line-item-budgets">(1) Line Item Budgets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-line-item-budgets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The expenditure are expressed in considerable details but activities being undertaken are given little attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It shows the nature of the spending but not the purpose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The amount in this type of budget are frequently established on the bases of historical costs that have been adjusted for anticipated changes in cost and activity levels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Control oriented – it is a form of financial control rather than effectiveness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shows exactly how much is spent on each item of expenditure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Focuses on ‘inputs’ not ‘outputs’ or ‘delivery’</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Itemizes payments (and receipts) by standard categories</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Helps to ensure aggregate fiscal discipline</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-and-disadvantages-of-line-item-budgets">Advantages and Disadvantages of Line Item Budgets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-and-disadvantages-of-line-item-budgets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Are simple to draw up</li>
<li>Provide an analysis of expenditure on inputs</li>
<li>Allow for easy control over inputs used</li>
<li>Easy for politicians to see an amount spent per budget item</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Provides little information about what the budget is spent on</li>
<li>Gives no indication of how funds are used within programmes</li>
<li>Does not show the differences in expenditures on managerial, administration and operational staff</li>
</ul>
<p>Focuses on control of funds instead of achieving results.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-programme-budgeting">2 Programme Budgeting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-programme-budgeting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Process that relates resources to proposed and actual results</li>
<li>Clusters of related activities that represent the highest level of classification of the work undertaken by a department in carrying out assigned responsibilities</li>
<li>Allocates money to functions/activities and focuses on total cost of providing a service, supported by line item detail.</li>
<li>Stresses on the end product, not the means</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-concepts-for-programmebased-budget-pbb">Key Concepts for programmebased Budget (PBB)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-concepts-for-programmebased-budget-pbb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vision: A realistic and attractive future scenario for the organization</p>
<p>Mission: A broad definition of why the agency exists, what are the main activities and who are the targeted beneficiaries</p>
<p>Programme:</p>
<ul>
<li>A group of independent but closely related services and activities which contribute to the programme goal.</li>
<li>A grouping of activities that contribute to a common strategic objective.</li>
<li>Programmes are divided into component sub-programmes</li>
</ul>
<p>Objectives of Programme Based Budget</p>
<ul>
<li>Making public management results-oriented</li>
<li>Improving efficiency/effectiveness of activities;</li>
<li>Using performance information for setting targets and priorities;</li>
<li>Guiding resource re-allocation with greater information;</li>
<li>Making efficiency savings wherever necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p>Line Item Budgeting vs. PBB</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Line Item Budgeting</th><th>PBB</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Focuses on compliance/use of inputs</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Presentation in terms of categories of inputs (line item)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>No information on performance</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>No information on unit costs of goods and services provided;</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Lack of information on future funding needs.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>No clear distinction between externally “administered” items (e.g., level of grants or subsidies) and “controlled” items (subject to managerial control)</td><td>Focuses on outputs/results</td></tr><tr><td>Presentation by activities/tasks performed (fewer appropriation items)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Performance measures defined</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Costing facilitated by defining outputs;</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Greater predictability in funding needs “Controlled” and “administered” items are identified and separately recorded</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Why Move to a PBB System?</p>
<ol>
<li>To improve efficiency and cost-effectiveness in public financial management using techniques and planning frameworks based on international best practice;</li>
<li>To improve resource allocation by identification, ranking and prioritization of programmes;</li>
<li>To improve the efficiency of budget management by including performance information in budget documents to assist monitoring and evaluation;</li>
<li>To use performance information to guide outlays on different activities, providing a more structured framework for budget resource allocation, both within and across sectors.</li>
</ol>
<p>Challenges of Programme Based Budgets</p>
<ul>
<li>Time consuming</li>
<li>Requires a lot of information</li>
<li>Requires a major change in the way a Ministry operates and change can be difficult</li>
<li>Requires a paradigm shift in management behaviour</li>
</ul>
<p>Financial Recording and Reporting Documents</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>General voucher</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>General allowance claim form</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Imprest request/retirement voucher</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cash reconciliation sheet:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monthly schedule of outstanding imprests</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>General ledger card</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cash book</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Quarterly budget expenditure report (QBER)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Final financial report</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Income register</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Budget is an estimate of Government expenditure and revenue presented to parliament by MoF before June 20th each year.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seeks approval for expenditures for the financial year that starts on 1st July for the vote of all</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Ministries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="budget-classification">Budget classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budget-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Recurrent Estimates (votes) for:
a. Services
b. Salaries</li>
<li>Development estimates (vote) for all development projects/programs/activities in all the ministries</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-budgets">Types of Budgets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-budgets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Medium-Term Expenditure Framework (MTEF): This is a three-year rolling budget process aimed at aligning policy, planning and budgeting.</p>
<p>Annual budget: An annual estimate of Government expenditures and revenues for all ministries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-revised-supplementary-budget">The Revised/Supplementary Budget<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-revised-supplementary-budget" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prepared in December of every year.</li>
<li>Enable ministries and departments adjust their budgetary allocation in line with the expenditure trends observed over the past six months.</li>
<li>Usually treasury only allows reallocations where savings can be realized from other expenditure areas.</li>
</ul>
<p>The budget preparation process</p>
<p>Sector Working Groups (SWGs)</p>
<ul>
<li>The MTEF process grouped ministries in economic divisions referred to as sectors.</li>
<li>Various ministries in a sector submit their budget proposals to the sector for funding (popularly known as bidding process).</li>
<li>The requests from the various ministries are evaluated by the Sector Working Groups (SWGs) which comprises officers from the respective ministries in the sector, Treasury and Ministry of Planning officials.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="confirm-this-conforms-to-new-constitution-requirement">Confirm this conforms to new Constitution requirement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#confirm-this-conforms-to-new-constitution-requirement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Ministerial Public Expenditure Review</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sector Working Groups</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sector Hearing Stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Annual Budget Preparation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Budget Statements</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="budget-implementation">Budget implementation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budget-implementation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>From 1st July (which year 2013 Ministries operate on Vote on Account whereby they are allowed to spend only one half of their provisions/ allocations until the Appropriation bill is passed</li>
<li>Field stations are given Authority to Incur Expenditures (AIES) and cheques / checks qu Sources of Government Finance/ revenue</li>
<li>GOV. Finance = All monies receivable by the Government for financing its services and implementation of development programmes</li>
<li>Classified into two:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Recurrent Revenue</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Finances needed to pay for the operating costs of running the government services.
Main sources of this revenue are:</li>
<li>Fines and fees</li>
<li>Taxes e.g. VAT, P.A.Y.E</li>
<li>Duties e.g. custom duty, excise duty</li>
<li>Investment revenue etc.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Appropriation in Aid</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Is a form of revenue that the Treasury allows an accounting officer to collect and use in addition to amounts issued from the exchequer.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Development Revenue</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Finances needed to implement development programmes and projects.
Main sources are:</li>
<li>Sale of non strategic assets</li>
<li>Grants</li>
<li>Loans quarterly in order to implement their planned activities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="budgeting-facility-level">Budgeting-Facility level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budgeting-facility-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☐ The budgetary process is carried out in tandem with the planning process.
☐ Technical and financial units work together in deriving costs of what is being proposed in the plan.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="budgeting-process">Budgeting Process:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budgeting-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Consider each objective separately.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Examine the approach accepted by the planning group noting the measures being proposed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Define the operational targets and specify the operational output and the quantification.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>List the activities, including support activities necessary to reach the operational targets, and quantify these activities. Assess the costs related to activities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Develop a table that shows for each stratum of the plan, the objectives, approaches (strategies), activities, targets and costs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply the costs of each target to a line-item budget format by categories (personnel, supplies, equipment, transportation, emergency funds for, say, malaria epidemic control and research).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prepare a clear presentation of the budget linked to the plan and be ready to defend it. Determine whether existing budgetary control procedures must undergo some changes and formulate recommendations for the proposed changes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Note the major budgetary implications of a decentralized organization.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Costs of large categories of activities may already be known from previous planning exercises or from a continuous programme of activity monitoring. If not, analyse tasks for major activity linked to every target and determine:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The time taken to accomplish every task.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The labour costs to estimate the staff needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The work that can be achieved in one day, one week, and one month.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The quantity and type of supplies and equipment required to accomplish the tasks and the costs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Factors that may assist and should be taken into account in assessing cost/efficiency are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Human resources relative to plans, and efficiency of human resources in relation to expectations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Financial resources intended for implementation and correct use of these resources.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Suitability of the sequence of activities and the appropriateness and timeliness of the logistical support.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Collaboration with other services in the health, social and economic sectors.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Applicability of operational plans.</p>
<ul>
<li>Work schedules.</li>
<li>The methods applied.</li>
<li>During the planning phase, the cost analysis will be stratified so as to permit analysis of each activity as well as of the programme as a whole. This operation may require additional human and other resources and may considerably increase the volume of reporting, but the results will permit substantial improvements in the programme's operating efficiency and considerable savings in the long term.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cash management</p>
<p>☑ Cash is the most important asset an organization can have. Its availability or lack of it can determine the success or failure of an organization.</p>
<p>Why manage cash?</p>
<p>☑ Inflows and outflows do not coincide i.e. cash needs vary.</p>
<p>☑ Cash is usually managed through preparation of a cash budget that can be prepared to capture the inflows and outflows on monthly basis for the next year and quarterly for second year.</p>
<p>Areas to monitor</p>
<p>☑ Imprests - especially for projects that require liquidation of advance before additional funds can be released.</p>
<p>☑ IOU's – they are illegal
☑ Substantial cash purchases – room for rent seeking
☑ The 'big three' i.e. Receivables, Payables and Inventory</p>
<p>UNIT FIVE: HUMAN RESOURCE MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>Purpose:</p>
<p>The purpose of this unit is to equip the learner with knowledge and skills in managing staff working in health records and information department</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-learning-outcomes">Expected learning outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-learning-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of the course, the learner should be able to;</p>
<ul>
<li>Define key concepts in human resources for health</li>
<li>Discuss the human resource health action framework</li>
<li>Discuss health policies and laws</li>
<li>Discuss the functional areas of human resources for health and plan HR requirements at local workplace</li>
<li>Apply the human resources norms and standards in health</li>
<li>Conduct effective performance appraisal in the workplace</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="course-overview">COURSE OVERVIEW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#course-overview" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Key concepts in human resources for health</li>
<li>Human Resource health action framework</li>
<li>Health policies and laws at global, national, county and institutional levels</li>

<li>Recruitment and Selection</li>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definitions-of-concepts">Definitions of concepts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions-of-concepts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Human resource management (HRM) is the systematic acquisition, maintenance, utilisation and outplacement of work force to achieve organisational objectives. It has several functional areas like planning, training and development, performance management amongst others.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="human-resources-for-health">Human resources for health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-resources-for-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Human resources for health management is the integrated use of policies, systems and management and leadership practices to plan for necessary staff and to recruit, motivate, develop, and maintain employees so that a health institution or organization can meet its goal. Source: USAID MSH e-handbook for Leaders and Managers (2010)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="components-of-hrm">Components of HRM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-hrm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>HR is the systematic acquisition, maintenance, utilization and outplacement of work force to achieve organizational objectives.</p>
<p>Consists of several functional areas:</p>
<ul>
<li>Human Resource Planning</li>
<li>Recruitment and selection</li>
<li>Training and development</li>
<li>Performance management</li>
<li>Compensation and rewards. HR is the systematic acquisition, maintenance, utilization and outplacement of work force to achieve organizational objectives.</li>
<li>Consists of several functional areas:</li>
<li>Human Resource Planning</li>
<li>Recruitment and selection</li>
<li>Training and development</li>
<li>Performance management</li>
<li>Compensation and rewards</li>
<li>Employee wellness</li>
<li>Employee relations</li>
<li>Retention and motivation</li>
<li>Exit management</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="human-resource-planning">Human Resource Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-resource-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The process through which an organization ensures determines current and future requirements of:</p>
<ul>
<li>the proper number of employees</li>
<li>appropriate skills</li>
<li>in the right jobs</li>
<li>at the right time to achieve organization's objectives.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="it-involves">It involves:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-involves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Job analysis</strong> refers to determining skills, duties, knowledge, tools, environment and the person required for job performance in the organization</li>
<li><strong>Staffing needs analysis</strong>—systematic reviewing human resource requirements to ensure that the required numbers of employees with the required skills and resources are available when needed</li>
<li>Human resource planning compares the present state of the organization with its goals for the future</li>
<li>Then identifies what changes it must make in its human resources to meet those goals</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recruitment-and-selection">Recruitment and selection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recruitment-and-selection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Recruitment</strong> is the process of searching the candidates for employment and stimulating them to apply for the jobs in the organization.</li>
<li>A process of finding and attracting capable applicants for employment.</li>
<li>It is the process of discovering sources of manpower to meet the requirement of staffing schedule and to employ effective measures for attracting the manpower in adequate numbers to facilitate effective selection of an effective workforce.</li>
<li>Searching for prospective employees</li>
<li><strong>Selection</strong> refers to choosing the most suitable candidates from those who apply for the job. It refers to offering jobs to desired candidates</li>
<li>A process of differentiating between applicants in order to identify and hire those with a greater likelihood of success in a job</li>
<li>A long process which begins with interview of applicants and ends with employment contract.</li>
<li>In practice selection differs from one organization to another and between different jobs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-and-development">Training and Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Deals with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Orientation and induction</li>
<li>Training &amp; development</li>
<li>Career planning &amp; Pathing</li>
<li>Career Counseling.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="orientation-and-induction">Orientation and Induction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orientation-and-induction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A procedure for providing new employees with basic background information about the firm such as rules</li>
<li>New employee orientation effectively integrates the new employee into your organization and assists with retention, motivation, job satisfaction, and quickly enabling each individual to become contributing members of the work team.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-and-development">Training and Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Training</strong> - refers to a learning experience organized by an employer to develop and sustain behaviors that bring about improvement and personal growth. It is organized for a specific period of time but outcomes can take long periods to be realized.</li>
<li>Training of employees is planned learning experience which provides staff with knowledge, attitudes and skills to enable them perform a specific job either today or in the future</li>
<li><strong>Development</strong> - learning that goes beyond today's current job needs, hence this includes training and education but goes beyond to target learning experiences which assist employees in personal life and growth</li>
<li>It prepares employees for future work, increase capacities to perform in the current jobs. e.g. preparing them for future challenges</li>
<li><strong>Career development</strong> - formal approach used by organization to ensure that people with proper qualification and experiences are available when needed</li>
<li><strong>Career planning</strong> - an ongoing process whereby an individual sets career goal and identify the means to achieve them</li>
<li><strong>Career pathing</strong> - identifying career goals and means to achieve them</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="process-of-training-and-development">Process of Training and Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#process-of-training-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The process takes the following steps:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-needs-assessment">Training Needs Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-needs-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Identifying gaps in knowledge and skills of workers which inhibit the performance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It aims at identifying critical skills gaps, develop a sound base for management decisions on training, realise demand driven training, improve overall performance and service delivery</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-projection">Training Projection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-projection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are plans based on identified training needs</li>
<li>They assist in preparation of projections that guide in nominations of officers for training</li>
<li>Aimed at developing HRD plans based on needs identified through the training needs assessment</li>
<li>It assists in earmarking those to be trained</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-budget">Training Budget<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-budget" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Financial implications of each course is taken into consideration depending on availability of funds</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="career-pathing">Career Pathing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#career-pathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Career path is a succession of different jobs through which an employee may move within an organisation. People move through their careers either upwards through promotion or by enriching their roles to utilise more skills</li>
<li>Career expectations of employees may differ significantly and therefore career paths should identify realistic options available within an organisation Career pathing</li>
<li>help employees identify skills required</li>
<li>align and integrate personal aspirations with organisational objectives</li>
<li>identify career paths that points in all directions, not only upwards</li>
<li>provide employees with the opportunity to develop themselves and their career</li>
<li>provide mutual benefits for both the organisation and individual</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="succession-planning">Succession planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#succession-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The planning takes into account the fact that employees will not remain indefinitely in the service of the organisation and provides a plan and process to deal with change that occur when employees leave</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The emphasis is on employee development, so that the organisation has a pool of qualified candidates who are willing to participate and contest for key positions or positions in key areas, if they become vacant Organisations should:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>assess their present and future needs based on their plans, strategic goals and objectives, or their priority programmes and projects</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>use the capabilities of existing employees to meet those needs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>develop a plan to fill the vacancies of those in authority who leave or are promoted</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Organisations should:</p>
<ul>
<li>assess their present and future needs based on their plans, strategic goals and objectives, or their priority programmes and projects</li>
<li>use the capabilities of existing employees to meet those needs</li>
<li>develop a plan to fill the vacancies of those in authority who leave or are promoted</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-to-consider-in-succession-planning">Steps to consider in succession planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-to-consider-in-succession-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Step 1 Identify key areas and key positions
Step 2 Identify capabilities for key areas and key positions
Step 3 Identify interested employees and assess them against capabilities
Step 4 Develop and implement succession and knowledge transfer plans
Step 5 Evaluate effectiveness</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="benefits-of-good-succession-planning">Benefits of good succession planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-good-succession-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Increases the level of employee engagement through career planning, a challenging work, training and development, career advancement and development horizontal</li>
<li>Improves the capacity of the organisation to achieve its business objectives through pools of qualified candidates for positions and key sectors</li>
<li>Allows managers to better appreciate the capabilities and skills, experience, diversity, language skills and interest in learning of their employees</li>
<li>Prevents the loss of institutional memory when employees leave the organisation</li>
<li>Allows for cost savings through the creation of a more committed and productive workforce</li>
<li>Creates a more efficient and effective public service in the long run</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="challenges-of-good-succession-planning">Challenges of good succession planning...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#challenges-of-good-succession-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Lack of discernment in the succession plan, we rely on employees who are not interested or motivated, and who have not qualified</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A lack of training and development will ensure that an employee will not be ready to get a promotion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A plan that does not promote employees in a timely manner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor communication of the succession plan could lead to confusion and turmoil within the organisation and staff</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="performance-management">PERFORMANCE MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#performance-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Performance management is a means of getting better results from the organisation, teams and individuals by understanding and managing performance within an agreed framework of planned goals, standards and competence requirements</li>
<li>It is a process of establishing shared understanding about what is to be achieved and an approach to managing and developing people in a way that increases probability that goals will be achieved in the long and shorter term and in the most efficient way</li>
<li>A process that consolidates goal setting, performance appraisal, and development into a single, common system, the aim of which is to ensure that the employee's performance is supporting the company's strategic aims</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-in-performance-management">Steps in performance management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-performance-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="role-definition">Role definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Agreeing on key result areas and competency requirements (Job descriptions)
Performance agreement (contract) or work plan</li>
<li>Objectives</li>
<li>Mechanism for measuring performance</li>
<li>Competencies needed to deliver required results</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="personal-development-plan">Personal development plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-development-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Intended actions for competency improvement for performance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Managing performance throughout the year</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking action to implement performance agreement and personal development plan (continuous feedback, informal progress reviews, updating objectives and counseling and remedial measures)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Performance review or appraisal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Formal evaluation stage (achievement, progress and problem/challenges)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If need be revision of performance agreements and personal development plans</p>
</li>
</ul>
