<p>This is a customer you can't see and must be handled carefully, has never complained.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-dictatorial-customer">The dictatorial Customer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-dictatorial-customer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Has a power complex and wishes to put you at a disadvantage. His/her actions are discourteous and intolerable.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-hesitant-suspicious-uncertain-customer">The hesitant/suspicious/uncertain Customer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-hesitant-suspicious-uncertain-customer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Is challengeable, uncertain and lacks confidence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-woman-type-or-men-type-customer">The 'woman' type (or men type!) customer.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-woman-type-or-men-type-customer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Focus on high quality with low price</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expectations-of-customers">Expectations of Customers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expectations-of-customers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Every time clients come for health services they have expectations. Consumer expectations are an important factor when considering improvement of health systems management. The product of Health Systems Management is consumer satisfaction, which can only be achieved if the following are observed in the interest of the client:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Speed and timeliness of service delivery/Punctuality</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Courtesy and helpfulness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Service reliability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Quality Service</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Consistency in service delivery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Accuracy of paperwork</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positive attitude from staff</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>User-friendly systems/</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>less bureaucracy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aesthetic environment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>In order to improve customer relationship management at any level, it is necessary to know your customers, their needs and expectations very well (Carlzon, 1989). At the same time it is important to be clear on your role in order to meet your consumer demand to the level of their expectation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-value-of-the-relationship">The Value of the Relationship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-value-of-the-relationship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Customer relationship management is about adding value to the relationship between the service provider and the client/customer. The result of value added relationship include increased loyalty of the customers, increased customers engagement in marketing the organization and finally improved performance and synergy on the basis of team spirit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-relationship-marketing-system">Internal Relationship Marketing System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-relationship-marketing-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Internal relationship management system recognizes the application of networking in working relationships between the organization and its customers. All employees are customers of managers who wish to carry out the departments' objectives.</p>
<p>The crucial aspects of internal relationship marketing system include the employer's engagement with those who create value as well as the need to brand the organization positively both inside and outside. Integrating psychological contract built from social capital reduces insecurity by filling in the gaps in the relationship not covered by a formal written employment contract. It is important to display commitment on the part of the organization to care for the personal and social needs of the employees who are customers of the managers who wish to carry out the firm's objectives.</p>
<p>UNIT EIGHT: DISASTER MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>Purpose</p>
<p>The purpose of this unit is to equip the learner with knowledge and skills in managing various types of disasters</p>
<p>Expected learning outcomes</p>
<p>At the end of this unit, the learner should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Define the various terms related to disaster management</li>
<li>Differentiate between disaster and hazard</li>
<li>Explain the elements of risk in relation to disaster management</li>
<li>Describe the types of disasters</li>
<li>Explain disaster management stages</li>
<li>Explain disaster management process</li>
<li>Describe the five (R) risk strategies involved in disaster management</li>
<li>Explain the effects of disasters on health</li>
<li>Describe vulnerability in relation to disaster management</li>
</ol>
<p>Common terminology used in disaster management</p>
<p>A Hazard: A hazard is a dangerous phenomenon, substance, human activity or condition that may cause the loss of life, injury or other health impacts, property damage, loss of livelihoods and services, social and economic disruption, or environmental damage.</p>
<p>A Natural Hazard: Natural processes or phenomenon that may cause loss of life, injury or other health impacts, property damage, loss of livelihoods and services, social and economic disruption, or environmental damage.</p>
<p>A Geological Hazard: Geological process or phenomenon that may cause loss of life, injury or other health impacts, property damage, loss of livelihoods and services, social and economic disruption, or environmental damage.</p>
<p>Technological Hazard: A hazard originating from technological or industrial conditions, including accidents, dangerous procedures, infrastructure failures or specific human activities, that may cause loss of life, injury, illness or other health impacts, property damage, loss of</p>
<p>livelihoods and services, social and economic disruption, or environmental damage.</p>
<p><strong>A Disaster:</strong> A disaster is a serious disruption of the functioning of a community or society causing widespread human, material, economic or environmental losses which exceed the ability of the affected community/society to cope using its own resources.</p>
<p><strong>A Disaster Risk:</strong> The potential disaster losses, in lives, health status, livelihoods, assets and services, which could occur to a particular community or a society over some specified future time period.</p>
<p><strong>Disaster Risk Management:</strong> The systematic process of using administrative directives, organizations, and operational skills and capacities to implement strategies, policies and improved coping capacities in order to lessen the adverse impacts of hazards and the possibility of disaster.</p>
<p><strong>Disaster Risk Reduction:</strong> The concept and practice of reducing disaster risk through systematic efforts to analyze and manage the causal factors of disasters, including through reduced exposure to hazards, lessened vulnerability of people and property, wise management of land and the environment, and improved preparedness for adverse events.</p>
<p><strong>Risk Assessment:</strong> A methodology to determine the nature and extent of risk by analyzing potential hazards and evaluating existing conditions of vulnerability that together could potentially harm exposed people, property, services, livelihoods and the environment on which they depend.</p>
<p><strong>Climate Change:</strong> A change in the state of the climate that can be identified (e.g. by using statistical tests) by changes in the mean and/or the variabilities of its properties and that persist for an extended period, typically decades or longer. Climate Change may be due to natural internal processes or external forcing or to persistent anthropogenic changes in the composition of the atmosphere or land use.</p>
<p>Adaptation to Climate Change: The adjustment in natural or human activities in responses to actual or expected climate stimuli or their effects which moderate harm or exploit beneficial opportunities.</p>
<p>Vulnerability: The characteristics and circumstances of a community, systemor asset that makes it susceptible to the damaging effects of a hazard.</p>
<p>Disaster occurs when a hazard results in devastation that leaves communities or even whole nations unable to cope unaided but disasters are neither inevitable nor 'natural'. There is no such thing as a 'natural' disaster. Many hazards are natural and usually inevitable, like cyclones, floods, droughts and earthquakes. They are 'hazards' in that they can potentially harm people, economies and the environment if they are not adequately prepared.</p>
<p>Moreover, the world has witnessed an alarming increase in the frequency and severity of disasters. Disaster cases are rising throughout the world due to a number of factors that include:</p>
<ul>
<li>more frequent extreme weather events</li>
<li>agricultural production systems that increase risk</li>
<li>population growth combined with demographic change and movements leading, for instance, unplanned urbanization, growing demand for food, industrial goods and services; and</li>
<li>Over-exploitation of natural resources.</li>
</ul>
<p>While better emergency response systems will save lives and properties, many of these losses can be avoided – or reduced – if appropriate policies and programmes are instituted to address the root causes and set in place mitigation, preparedness and response mechanisms that are effectively integrated into overall development planning.</p>
<p>These issues were debated during the World Conference on Disaster Reduction (WCDR) in Kobe, Hyogo, Japan (January 2005). It was therefore insisted on the need to move from theory to concrete action in disaster risk reduction.</p>
<p>Hazard and Disaster:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>closely related terms</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, a hazard is a natural event while the disaster is its consequence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hazard refers to the event which may cause disaster</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They could be either man-made or naturally occurring hazards in our environment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Disaster is combination of two words: ‘des’ meaning evil and ‘astre’ meaning star</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Disaster therefore means evil star. A complete definition of disaster provided by Turner (1976) as ‘an event, concentrated in time and space, which threatens a society or a subdivision of a society with major unwanted consequences as a result of the collapse of precautions which had hitherto been culturally accepted as adequate’</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Common definition: major misfortune which disrupts the normal functioning of the society</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Emergency:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The term ‘emergency’ is used to describe the crisis which a community has great difficulty to cope with</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>External assistance is needed to cope with the emergencies</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>political emergency, drought, famine etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Calamity:
Calamity is defined as deep distress, disaster to a lesser degree of damage, which disrupts the normal functioning of the people of a society</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vulnerability:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>“Vulnerability” basically means susceptibility of a population or system (e.g., a hospital, water supply and sewage system, or aspects of infrastructure) to the effects of the hazard</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>“The extent to which a community, structure, service or geographic area is likely to be damaged or disrupted by the impact of particular disaster hazard...”</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Its magnitude is expressed on a scale from 0.0 (No damage or loss) to 1.0 (total loss).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The probability that a particular system or population will be affected by hazards is known as the “risk.”</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk is a function of the vulnerability and the hazard, and is expressed as follows:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk = Vulnerability x Hazard. It means, the risk increases if the vulnerability of the population or the systems is more; and also of the magnitude of the hazard is more.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-76f20f6a.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characterization-of-disasters">Characterization of Disasters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characterization-of-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-disasters">Types disasters:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Various types of disasters have been categorized under five sub groups</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Sub-Group 1: Water and Climate Related Hazards.</strong>
(i) Floods, (ii) Droughts, (iii) Cyclones, (iv) Tornadoes &amp; Hurricanes, (v) Hailstorm, (vi) Cloudburst, (vii) Snow Avalanches, (viii) Heat &amp; Cold Waves, (ix) Sea Erosion, (x) Thunder and Lightening</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Sub-Group 2: Geologically related Hazards</strong>
Earthquakes, (ii) Landslides, (iii) Mudflows, (iv) Dam Bursts, (v) Dam Failures</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Sub-Group 3: Chemical, Industrial &amp; Nuclear related Disasters</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sub-Group 4: Accident Related Disasters.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Road, Rail and other Transportation accidents, (ii) Major Building Collapse, (iii) Serial Bomb Blasts, (iv) Festival related Disasters, (v) Fires, (vi) Forest Fires</p>
<ul>
<li>Sub-Group 5: Biologically Related Disasters</li>
</ul>
<p>(i) Biological Disasters, (ii) Epidemics, (iii) Cattle Epidemics, (iv) Pest Attacks, (v) Food Poisoning</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="similarly-disasters-can-be-classified-as-follows">Similarly, disasters can be classified as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#similarly-disasters-can-be-classified-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Anthropogenic hazards: These are human made hazards such as
a. anthropogenic pollutant hazards which come as a result of transformation of the nature by human beings e.g. production of chemical,
b. anthropogenic pollutant hazards which come as a result of transformation of nature by human being e.g. nuclear plant, industrial pollution</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Environmental degradation. These hazards can be anthropogenic, socio-natural or natural</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Biological hazards. These hazards include anthropogenic, socio-natural or natural. Examples are: epidemics, pandemics, locusts bioterrorism/biological weapons</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Geological/geotectonic origin: The category include land movement, volcanoes, earthquake and tsunami</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Geological/geomorphism origin: These include land slide, avalanche/snow slide, land and coastal erosion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Meteorological and climate origin: The include hurricanes, tropical storms and tornadoes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hydraulic origin: food, water stagnation</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The last two can be combined together as hydro-meteorological</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Socio-natural hazards. Examples are: Flood, Desertification, Drought, Deforestation, Climate change and Global warming</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occupational/ergonomic hazards. These are occupational accidents arising due to work position at work place.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical hazards: these are heat, cold, global warming and climate change</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mechanical hazards. These are accidents</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychological hazards. Examples are stress, schizophrenia, anxiety, depression and mental disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Agricultural hazards. Pesticides, fertilizers</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-understanding-hazard">What is understanding hazard?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-understanding-hazard" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Understanding hazard involves:</p>
<ul>
<li>How hazards arise</li>
<li>Probability of occurrence and magnitude</li>
<li>Physical mechanism of destruction</li>
<li>E.g. In earthquakes, most fatalities are due to building collapse. Focus should be on prevention of building collapse</li>
<li>In floods, death occurs due to drowning in fast flowing currents. Focus is on limiting the exposure of people by keeping them out of track of water</li>
<li>Elements most vulnerable</li>
<li>Consequence of damage</li>
<li>Damage to factory can lead to jobless people</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims-of-disaster-management">AIMS OF DISASTER MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims-of-disaster-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reduce (Avoid, if possible) the potential losses from hazards.</li>
<li>Assure prompt and appropriate assistance to victims when necessary.</li>
<li>Achieve rapid and durable recovery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stages-of-disaster-management">Stages of disaster management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-disaster-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pre-disaster phase: taken prior to the occurrence of any disasters. For. E.g. Construction of buildings which can withstand the impact of disaster. It is also called 'mitigation phase'.</li>
<li>Actual disaster phase: During this phase, timely warning is to be given to the people so that they can timely take action to face the disaster. It is also called the 'preparatory phase'.</li>
<li>Post-disaster phase: It includes the measures that are taken after the</li>
</ul>
<p>occurrence of a disaster. It further includes three phases:</p>
<ul>
<li>Relief phase: immediately after the occurrence of a disaster.</li>
<li>Rehabilitation phase: to rehabilitate the community through the development of house, restoring water supply, sanitation, food and providing loans so that the people are brought back to the normal work.</li>
<li>Reconstruction Phase: It involves developing new colonies to make the disaster affected people to settle permanently.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-11350ae4.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="five-r-strategy">"Five-R Strategy"<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#five-r-strategy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disaster management is based on "Five-R Strategy" of</p>
<ul>
<li>Rescue</li>
<li>Relief</li>
<li>Restoration</li>
<li>Rehabilitation</li>
<li>Reconstruction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disaster-risk-management">Disaster risk management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disaster-risk-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparatory-phase">Preparatory phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparatory-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The preparatory phase of disaster response includes all of the activities that help a society and the disaster agencies to prepare for a disaster event. These activities are broadly classified as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>disaster prevention:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The objective of prevention is to prevent the disaster from occurring.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>disaster mitigation:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disaster mitigation accepts that some natural event may occur, but it tries to lessen the impact by improving the common ability.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>disaster preparedness:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disaster preparedness assumes that a disaster will occur; it focuses on structuring the emergency response and on laying a framework for recovery.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disaster-mitigation">Disaster mitigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disaster-mitigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disaster Mitigation is essentially measures taken in advance of a disaster aimed at minimizing or eliminating the impact of disaster on community and environment.</li>
<li>2 components: reducing hazard and reducing vulnerability.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reducing-hazard-vs-reducing-vulnerability">Reducing hazard vs reducing vulnerability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reducing-hazard-vs-reducing-vulnerability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Reducing hazard:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>protection against threat by removing the cause of threat</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eg. Construction of levees along banks of river to reduce chance of flooding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tree plantation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Reducing vulnerability:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>reducing the effect of threat</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eg. Constructing buildings as per bylaws in NBC</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most of the natural hazards are unpreventable, therefore, we mostly work towards reducing vulnerability.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disaster-mitigation-measures">Disaster Mitigation Measures:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disaster-mitigation-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Passive mitigation measure</li>
</ul>
<p>Active mitigation measures</p>
<p>Authorities prevent undesired actions through controls and penalties by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Requirement to conform with design codes</li>
<li>Checking compliance of controls on-site</li>
<li>Imposing court proceedings, fines, closure orders on offenders</li>
<li>Control of land use</li>
<li>Denial of utilities and infrastructure to areas where development is undesired</li>
<li>Compulsory insurance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirements-of-passive-control-systems">Requirements of passive control systems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements-of-passive-control-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. An existing and enforceable system of control
b. Acceptance by the affected community of the objectives and the authority imposing the controls
c. The economic capability of the affected community to comply with the regulations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="active-mitigation-measures">Active mitigation measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#active-mitigation-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Authorities promote desired actions through incentives like:</p>
<ul>
<li>Planning control dispensations</li>
<li>Training and education</li>
<li>Economic assistance (grants and preferential loans)</li>
<li>Subsidies on safety equipment, safer building materials, etc.</li>
<li>Provision of facilities: safer buildings, refuge points, storage</li>
<li>Public information dissemination and awareness raising</li>
<li>Promotion of voluntary insurance</li>
<li>Creation of community organizations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="active-programs">Active Programs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#active-programs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Aim to create a self-perpetuating safety culture in areas of weak authority or poor ability to comply with existing controls.
b. Require large budgets, skilled manpower and extensive administration.
c. Are useful in areas of low income, rural areas or elsewhere where there is no external jurisdiction over land use or building activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phases-of-disaster-mitigation">Phases of disaster mitigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phases-of-disaster-mitigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk analysis</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention
Preparedness</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-analysis">Risk Analysis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>What is risk?</li>
<li>Expected loss caused by a particular phenomenon</li>
<li>Risk analysis:</li>
<li>Process of determining the nature and scale of losses which can be anticipated in a particular area.</li>
<li>It involves analysis of</li>
<li>the probability of a hazard of a particular magnitude occurring (called hazard assessment)</li>
<li>the elements susceptible to potential loss or damage (called elements at risk)</li>
<li>the nature of vulnerability of those elements (vulnerability analysis), and a specified future time period (loss estimation)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hazard-assessment">Hazard assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazard-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The process of estimating the probability of occurrence of a damaging phenomenon of given magnitude in a given area</li>
<li>Based on collection of historical and scientific data</li>
<li>Points to be considered in Hazard assessment:</li>
<li>History</li>
<li>Probability of various intensities</li>
<li>Maximum threat</li>
</ul>
<p>Possible secondary hazards: eg. Earthquake can cause dam burst</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="elements-at-risk">Elements at risk:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elements-at-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>People: loss of life,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Personal health: injury or disease,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Damage, destruction of property,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Damage, destruction of infrastructure, public service systems,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Damage, destruction of environment,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Damage, destruction of crops,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption, loss of production,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption, loss of livelihood,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption, loss of essential services,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption, loss of national infrastructure,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption to governmental process, systems,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss to national, local economies,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disruption, loss of community or lifestyle, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sociological and psychological consequences.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-disaster-on-health">Effects of disaster on health:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-disaster-on-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Population density</li>
<li>Population displacement</li>
<li>Disruption and contamination of water supply and sanitation services</li>
<li>Disruption of public health programme</li>
<li>Economic changes that favour breeding of factors</li>
<li>Displacement of domestic and wild animals</li>
<li>Provision of emergency food, water and shelter in disaster situation</li>
<li>Climate change and health issues</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disaster-building-block">Disaster building block:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disaster-building-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Disaster/impact</li>
<li>Response</li>
<li>Rehabilitation</li>
<li>Reconstruction</li>
<li>Mitigation</li>
<li>Preparedness</li>
</ol>
<p>In comprehensive emergency management model (CEMM), there should be disaster preparedness in such a way that if there is a disaster, there is effective disaster response and therefore, able to deal effectively with rehabilitation and reconstruction. Moreover, disaster mitigation is crucial in dealing with disaster.</p>
<p>Vulnerability analysis:</p>
<ul>
<li>A process which results in an understanding of the types and levels of exposure of persons, property, and the environment to the effects of identified hazards at a particular time.</li>
<li>Vulnerability = People + Condition + Place + Time + Event</li>
<li>vulnerability also differs according to intensity of the hazard</li>
</ul>
<p>Types of Vulnerability:</p>
<ul>
<li>Physical Vulnerability</li>
<li>Economic</li>
<li>Social</li>
<li>environmental</li>
</ul>
<p>Physical Vulnerability:</p>
<ul>
<li>pertaining to matters of location, structural and infrastructural conditions etc</li>
</ul>
<p>Includes</p>
<ul>
<li>Buildings at risk</li>
<li>Unsafe infrastructure: eg. Transportation system, sanitation system etc.</li>
<li>Unsafe critical facilities</li>
<li>Rapid urbanization</li>
<li>Agricultural-primarily considering physical assets-related, but opportunity loss potential of essential natural resources, crops, trees, livestock, fisheries, also should be recognized.</li>
</ul>
<p>Economic Vulnerability:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Determined by evaluating</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the direct loss potential of economic assets</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>indirect loss potential</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>secondary effects</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Direct Loss Potential</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>destruction of buildings, plants, facilities, raw material, products,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Replacement costs,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss of employment,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Crop losses, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Damage to means of production.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Indirect Loss Potential</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impact of lost production,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impact of lost employment,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss of markets,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss of opportunity,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss to consequential income-earning activities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Secondary Effects</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inflation,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indebtedness,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Labour migration,</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Social Vulnerability:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>determined by the perception of risk and the ability of people to take measures to reduce that risk</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>more difficult to measure than either physical or economic vulnerability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Critical Indicators of Perceived Risk, Ability of Response:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poverty, limitation of resources, reserves or options,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Degree of public awareness about the immediate social and physical environments</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prior personal experience of specific risk, consequence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Demographic Considerations:</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Magnitudes, total population,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Concentration densities,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Demographic distinctions, vulnerable groups of socially disadvantaged people or those requiring special attention. These include children, disabled, elderly people, women</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Capabilities:</strong>
When conducting vulnerability analysis, special note should be taken of positive attributes able to be identified that may contribute to an enhanced ability to prevent or</p>
<p>mitigate the effects of a disaster, or which may strengthen a community's ability to respond effectively to the hazard</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="technocratic-view-for-managing-the-risk">Technocratic view for managing the risk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#technocratic-view-for-managing-the-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Problem-Physical vulnerability</li>
<li>Symptoms as perceived- High death toll and damages of infrastructure attribute to severity of hazard, extensive and recurrent rehabilitation needs.</li>
<li>The causes-uncontrolled characteristics of hazard events, physiography of the prone areas, lack of inadequacy of protective infrastructure, failure of forecasting and warning.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-management-process">Risk Management Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-management-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Risk management has three components namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Risk identification</li>
<li>Risk reduction</li>
<li>Risk transfer</li>
</ul>
<p>Risk identification has to be done through mapping and using other available technological options</p>
<p>It is usual to allocate risk management to special body at national level. Usually, it is a national disaster management organization at national level. Others support should be obtained within a National Action Plan for disaster management.</p>
<p>At local, it may be the responsibility of a disaster mitigation committee, which administers risk management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-reduction">Risk reduction:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-reduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Effective risk reduction involves mitigation measures in hazard prone areas. It may also involve overcoming the socio-economic, institutional and political barriers to the adoption of effective risk reduction strategies and measures in developing countries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-management">Risk Management:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process by which assessed risks are mitigated, minimized or controlled through engineering, management of land use prances or other operational means. This involves</p>
<p>the optimal allocation of available resources in support of group goals</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-transfer">Risk Transfer:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-transfer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Effective risk transfer involves different tools such as insurances; tax policies special measures focused on land management. Organizational structures, policies, legislation etc is required for effective implementation of risk transfer strategies for a country or local government areas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-in-hazard-analysis">Steps in Hazard analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-hazard-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Understand the type and nature of hazard</li>
<li>Collect the data from history about frequency, duration, controllability etc.</li>
<li>Vulnerability analysis: physical, economic etc.</li>
<li>Strategies to minimize vulnerability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disaster-mitigation-actions">Disaster Mitigation Actions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disaster-mitigation-actions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Engineering and construction</li>
<li>Engineered buildings</li>
<li>Non-engineered</li>
<li>Existing buildings</li>
<li>Physical planning</li>
<li>Location of public sector units</li>
<li>Provision of several small facilities</li>
<li>Changing use of vulnerable buildings</li>
<li>Availability of safer land for poorer community</li>
<li>Economic</li>
<li>Diversification of economy: single type of industry is vulnerable</li>
<li>Economic incentives like loans, tax concessions etc.</li>
<li>Management and institutional</li>
<li>Special department for disaster management</li>
<li>Societal</li>
<li>Public awareness through education</li>
<li>Involvement of community through drills</li>
</ul>
<p>Assignment/sample questions</p>
<ol>
<li>Map out disasters in Kenya for the last 10 years</li>
<li>Describe the trends of various disasters in Kenya for the last 10 years</li>
<li>Identify the current Kenyan legislations on disaster management</li>
<li>Explain the application of compressive emergency management model</li>
<li>Describe the following in relation to disaster management:
a. Disaster
b. Response
c. Rehabilitation
d. Reconstruction
e. Mitigation and
f. Preparedness</li>
</ol>
<p>UNIT 9: PROJECT MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>Purpose</p>
<p>This unit covers the project management cycle and endeavors to equip learners with information and skills on different aspects of project management.</p>
<p>Specific Objectives</p>
<ul>
<li>Define project management concepts</li>
<li>Describe the purpose of a healthcare project proposal</li>
<li>Identify and discuss the major stages in project cycle</li>
<li>Recognize the essential elements of a project proposal.</li>
<li>Describe the organization and administration of the project</li>
</ul>
<p>Planning</p>
<p>Planning is making decisions about which courses of action to follow. It is the root to objective where it involves conceptualizing and anticipating future action</p>
<p>It includes the following activities:</p>
<ul>
<li>Establishing objectives to determine the end result;</li>
<li>Developing strategies to determine how to reach objectives, by when, and by whom;</li>
<li>Preparing budgets to determine the cost of using resources;</li>
<li>Establishing policies to have standing decisions on recurring situations;</li>
<li>Establishing standards to ensure continued quality of services and products.</li>
</ul>
<p>Importance of planning</p>
<ul>
<li>Gives a sense of direction.</li>
<li>Focuses attention on objectives.</li>
<li>Involve others – participation, teamwork.</li>
<li>Helps anticipate problems and cope with any change in an organization.</li>
<li>Enhances appropriate allocation of resources.</li>
<li>Helps in coordination</li>
<li>Leads to more effectiveness and efficiency of services</li>
</ul>
<p>Key elements of planning</p>
<ul>
<li>Knowing where we are (Situation)</li>
<li>Deciding where we want to go (Vision/Objectives)</li>
<li>What do we need to reach where we want to go (Resources)</li>
<li>How we are going there (Method/process/how)</li>
<li>Deciding how far we can get towards your target in a period of time (Time line/When)</li>
<li>How will we know when we get there?</li>
</ul>
<p>This requires the development of measurable indicators for monitoring progress and evaluating results</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>How far we have gone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where we are not on target</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How we can do better in future</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amending the implementation plan (RE-planning)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-planning-cycle">THE PLANNING CYCLE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-planning-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>How will we know when we get there?
(Monitoring and evaluation, including choice and setting of appropriate indicators)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-59ab076e.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p>Where are we now? (Identify needs and problems)</p>
<p>Where do we want to go? What is the vision? (Set priorities and targets)</p>
<p>How will we get there?
(Develop interventions and identify resources)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-should-plan">Who should plan?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-should-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Planning should be a participatory process</p>
<ul>
<li>Community / key stakeholders must be involved through the process, e.g. in doing the contextual and situational analysis, setting priorities e.t.c.</li>
<li>Basic components of every organization with which the manager must work are people, things and ideas.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rationale-for-participatory-planning">Rationale for Participatory planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rationale-for-participatory-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Mobilization and allocation of resources to different health problems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Participation is open-ended hence allows greater participation (Ownership and sustainability)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Guide the anticipation of potential constraints and solutions to achieving the vision – systematic and predictable way</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Promote synergy and greater coordination of health problems in a multi-stakeholders’ environment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-steps-in-planning">Key Steps in Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-steps-in-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Situation analysis</li>
<li>Setting priority</li>
<li>Options appraisal</li>
<li>Programming</li>
<li>Implementation and Monitoring</li>
<li>Evaluation</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="situation-analysis">Situation analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#situation-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Improving the understanding of the current situation in order to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide a common reference point for the planning process</li>
<li>Allow the selection of priority areas of concern for planning</li>
</ul>
<p>SA outlines and assesses 3 broad areas</p>
<ul>
<li>Demographic situation and health needs</li>
<li>Services and resources</li>
<li>Socioeconomic Status</li>
<li>Health related services of other sectors</li>
<li>Geographic and topographic pattern</li>
<li>Present infrastructure and service pattern</li>
<li>Existing service resources</li>
<li>Effectiveness and efficiency of current services</li>
<li>Policy and political environment (General, Govt. Policies)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="setting-priority">Setting priority<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#setting-priority" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Making choices among major needs so as to allocate resources efficiently.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Consider the following in setting priority</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Magnitude of the issue/Problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Who is determining the needs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Target group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cost, ease and effectiveness of intervention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Political context</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="options-appraisal">Options appraisal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#options-appraisal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Process of deciding between alternative approaches to achieve an objective</li>
<li>Determine the objectives of the activity being appraised</li>
<li>Identify alternative options (exclude unfeasible and uneconomical option)</li>
<li>Identify resources required to achieve each option and the benefit of each option</li>
<li>Cost the resources required</li>
<li>A good option appraisal should;</li>
<li>Present quantifiable and non-quantifiable costs and benefits</li>
<li>Explicitly recognize and incorporate the need for other perspective</li>
<li>Recognize the resource and financial implication</li>
<li>Examine the technical feasibility</li>
<li>Consider the process effects</li>
<li>Set out information on the methodology used</li>
<li>Perform where necessary sensitivity analysis</li>
<li>Set out key assumptions</li>
<li>Use of sustainability Grid</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="programming">Programming<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#programming" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Budgeting and Developing of a plan of action</li>
<li>This process is carried out for each priority area and its associated set of targets.</li>
<li>It translates the results of the earlier decisions into a series of programs each with a budget and resources</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-planning-tools">Common Planning Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-planning-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Logical Framework</li>
<li>Gantt Charts</li>
<li>Activity Schedule</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="logical-framework">Logical Framework<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#logical-framework" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A tool to help designers of projects think logically about:</p>
<ul>
<li>what the project is trying to achieve (Purpose),</li>
<li>what things the project need to do to bring that about (Outputs)</li>
<li>what needs to be done to produce these outputs (Activities)</li>
<li>What is required to implement the activities (Input)</li>
<li>What potential problems could affect the success of the project</li>
<li>How the progress and ultimate success of the project will be measured</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Objectives</th><th>Objectively Verifiable Indicators</th><th>Means of Verification</th><th>Assumptions and Risks</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Overall Goal</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Project Purpose</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Results / Outputs</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Activities</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-log-frame">Advantages of Log Frame<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-log-frame" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It brings together in one place a statement of all the key components of a project</li>
<li>It presents them in a systematic, concise and coherent way, thus clarifying and exposing the logic of how the project is expected to work</li>
<li>It separates out the various levels in the hierarchy of objectives, helping to ensure that inputs and outputs are not confused with each other or with objectives and that wider</li>
</ul>
<p>ranging objectives are not overlooked</p>
<ul>
<li>It clarifies the relationships which underlie judgments about likely efficiency and effectiveness of projects</li>
<li>It identifies the main factors related to the success of the project</li>
<li>It provides a basis for monitoring and evaluation by identifying indicators of success, and means of quantification or assessment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gantt-charts">Gantt Charts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gantt-charts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A special chart used by project planners to illustrate the project schedule from the start to the end</li>
<li>Shows the broad work breakdown structure of a project</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="project-activity-schedule">Project Activity Schedule<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#project-activity-schedule" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Simple Matrix outlining the specific activities, when they will be done, who is responsible and resources required.</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>What(Activity)</th><th>Where (Site)</th><th>When (Time Frame)</th><th>Who (Responsible person)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="budgeting">Budgeting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#budgeting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Determination of cost of inputs and activities required to implement a plan</li>
<li>Personnel costs</li>
<li>Non labor charges: equipment, travel, reproduction of materials, computer use, office space, supplies etc</li>
<li>Administrative costs</li>
<li>Overheads eg. Staff benefits etc</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implementation-and-monitoring">Implementation and monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implementation-and-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Implementation is the process of transforming the broad program into more specific timed</p>
<p>and budgeted sets of tasks and activities. It is the action portion of the plan. Drawing up a more operational plan or a work plan and taking action accordingly. Implementation involves securing community participation for launching the project, co-ordination of activities, monitoring, and taking care of contingencies. Project implementation includes various management functions including</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Co-ordination</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organizing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Staffing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Controlling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Team-building</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contingency Management</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring – Continuous assessment of the progress of an activities over time. Observers whether an activity or service is occurring as planned based on activity plans and schedules</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>A good monitoring system ensures that the programme interventions stay on course by:</p>
<ul>
<li>checking that activities are implemented</li>
<li>measuring progress towards objectives</li>
<li>identifying problems as they come up</li>
<li>identifying strengths that can be built on.</li>
<li>adapting to changing circumstances.</li>
<li>It uses the systematic collection of data on specified indicators to inform management and the main stakeholders of an ongoing operation of the extent of progress and achievement of results in the use of allocated funds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="evaluation">EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: Evaluation means measurement, appraisal, or making judgments on the output and impact of the project in terms of the objectives.</p>
<p>It is the periodic assessment of the relevance, performance, efficiency, effectiveness, impact and sustainability, and benefits to the target community</p>
<p>Evaluations are conducted to determine whether a project has met its objective/goals.</p>
<p>The process of determining whether the program is achieving its purpose, whether it should be continued or terminated, and how it can be improved or better managed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-evaluation">The purpose of evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To improve health programmes and the services of delivering them</li>
<li>Guide the allocation of financial and human resources</li>
<li>Provides a basis for the next assessment hence a fresh lead in to the planning spiral</li>
<li>Evaluation is used to determine whether</li>
<li>The activities were worth carrying out</li>
<li>The activity should be continued or not</li>
<li>It accomplished the objectives it set out to achieve</li>
<li>It should be extended here or elsewhere</li>
<li>Modification of the activity might make a difference to its performance</li>
<li>To justify spending on an activity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="evaluation-cycle">EVALUATION CYCLE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Definethepurpose of the evaluation</li>
</ol>
<p>Who wants the evaluation, why and what how are they going to use the results</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Define the priority areas to be evaluated. This includes the most important area to be evaluated – e.g. projects’ progress towards reaching its goals and objectives, technical aspects and so on</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Information collection plan: Use the focus areas and list:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>What key factors (indicators) will be researched on each area,</p>
<p>The source of information (i.e. the data collection tool and where that information is to be found)</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>The implementation plan.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Decide who will participate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Make a budget.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A list of participants,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Detailed calendar of tasks and responsibilities, including a target date for report completion,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If instruments (interviews, surveys, etc.) are needed, these can be designed immediately after the planning session, and field-tested according to the plan.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-analyse-and-organize-the-information">5. Analyse and organize the information.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-analyse-and-organize-the-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>How is the information to be analysed and by whom? Who will develop the final conclusions and recommendations? Make an outline of the final report. Decide how much data will be needed, and what limits of time and other resources affect the work of tabulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-communicating-the-findings-and-making-follow-up">6. Communicating the findings and making follow-up<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-communicating-the-findings-and-making-follow-up" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A follow-up plan should include</p>
<p>a). An agreement on specific tasks/actions to be taken by the donor agency, the project implementer, and the beneficiary organization to meet the evaluation's recommendations,
b). Designation of persons to do each follow-up activity,
c). An estimate of dates for implementing each activity
d). The date when the activity is to be completed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-evaluation">Types of evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-process-evaluation">1. Process evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-process-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Internal evaluation – periodic self evaluation of a project including review of goals, strategies and work plans. Answers the questions about : HOW the program is implemented and how the outcomes are achieved</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="components-of-process-evaluation">Components of process evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-process-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Relevance</strong> – rationale for adopting the community based health care policies and practices.</p>
<p>Measures the response of the project to essential human needs and social and health policies and priorities</p>
<p><strong>Adequacy</strong> – sufficient attention has been paid to certain previously determined courses of</p>
<p>action</p>
<p><strong>Process</strong> – comparison of actual with scheduled activities, the identification of reasons for achievements or short comings and indications for remedies for any shortcomings
Purpose is to facilitate the monitoring and operational control of on going activities</p>
<p><strong>Efficiency</strong> – an expression of the relationship between results obtained from a health program or activity and the efforts expended in terms of human, financial and other resources. – aims at improving implementation</p>
<p><strong>Effectiveness</strong> – expression of the desired effect of a program, service institution or support activity in reducing a health problem. Measures the degree of attainment</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-impact-evaluation">2. Impact evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-impact-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Aims at identifying any necessary change in the direction of health programs so as to increase their contribution to overall health and socioeconomic development.</p>
<ul>
<li>Impact evaluation measures whether or not a project achieved its goals and attempts to see what impact the project had on participants</li>
<li>An independent consultant may conduct the impact evaluation</li>
<li>Scope includes all stake holders – donor agency, international cooperating agency, local project organization and the beneficially community</li>
</ul>
<p>an expression of the overall effect of a program, service or institution on health and related socio-demographic development</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indicators-for-evaluation">INDICATORS FOR EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indicators-for-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Indicators</strong> are variables that help to measure changes.</p>
<p>The indicators for evaluation include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health policy indicators which include</li>
<li>Political commitment</li>
<li>Resource allocation</li>
<li>Degree of equitable distribution of the resources</li>
<li>Level of community involvement</li>
<li>Social and economic indicators</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benefits-of-program-evaluation">BENEFITS OF PROGRAM EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-program-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Reflect on progress; see where we are going and where we are coming from and improve programs</li>
<li>Influence policy makes and funders</li>
<li>Build community capacity and engage communities</li>
<li>Benefits of program evaluation</li>
<li>Share what works and what doesn't work with other communities</li>
<li>Ensure funding and sustainability</li>
<li>Strengthen accountability</li>
</ul>
